Rain taps softly against the crooked shingles of the hut.

The trader’s wagon wheels creak to a stop in the mud outside. Through a crack in the wooden wall you can see the faint orange glow of lanternlight cutting through the dark forest. The air smells of wet leaves, woodsmoke… and something bitter. Herbs, maybe. Or something worse.

The trader’s hand clamps around the back of your neck and drags you down from the wagon.

Your feet hit the mud.

You’re small even for a kobold — thin arms, narrow chest, scales still soft with youth. The rope around your wrists rubs raw as he jerks you forward.

Ahead stands the hut.

It leans slightly to one side as if tired of standing. Twisted branches hang from cords across the doorway. Bones. Feathers. Dried plants tied in tight bundles.

Something chimes softly in the wind.

The door creaks open before the trader even knocks.

A woman stands in the doorway.

Tall. Thin. Hair the color of ash hangs loose over her shoulders. Her eyes reflect the lanternlight like a cat’s. Around her neck hang dozens of small charms — teeth, shells, carved bits of wood.

And gems.

Small ones.

She looks down at you the way someone looks at a tool they’re considering buying.

The trader clears his throat.

“Found you one,” he says.

She crouches slowly in front of you. Her long fingers lift your chin, turning your head left… then right.

Her nails are cold.

“Mmm.”

A faint smile touches her lips.

“Still young. Good.”

She stands and tosses the trader a small leather pouch. It jingles.

The trader doesn’t even look at you again. Coins are counted. The deal is done.

Your village is already gone from the trader’s mind.

The witch grips the rope around your wrists and pulls you inside the hut.

The door closes.

Inside, the air is thick with incense and damp rot. Shelves line the walls, cluttered with jars. Some hold herbs. Some hold things that used to be alive.

A low fire crackles beneath an iron cauldron.

She unties your wrists.

Not kindly — just efficiently.

Then she gestures toward the floor near the hearth.

“Sit.”

Her voice is calm. Matter-of-fact. Like she’s telling someone where to place a chair.

Outside, the trader’s wagon rolls away into the rain.

You are alone with her now.

The witch begins grinding something in a stone mortar, humming softly to herself.

The hut creaks in the wind.

The smell of smoke and strange powders fills your nose.

After a moment, she glances at you again.

Waiting.

What do you do?
Obey and sit quietly near the fire, trying not to draw attention.
Ask her what she plans to do with you.
Look around the hut carefully, studying the jars, tools, and doorways.
Attempt to run for the door while her back is turned.
Bare your teeth and refuse to cooperate, showing defiance.

(You may also choose any other action.)

The hut is warm compared to the rain outside.

You lower yourself to the dirt floor beside the hearth. The packed earth is warm where the fire has baked it for years. Ash dusts your claws as you sit.

The witch keeps grinding the mixture in the stone bowl.

scrape… scrape… scrape…

Your voice is small when it leaves your throat.

“I… want to go home…”

The grinding stops.

The hut creaks in the wind.

For a moment she says nothing.

Then she laughs.

Not loudly. Not cruelly. Just… amused.

A dry, breathy sound.

She turns her head slightly, looking down at you over one shoulder. The firelight dances across the wrinkles around her eyes.

“Oh, little scale…”

She wipes the powder from the mortar into a clay dish.

“Home sold you.”

She says it the way someone might mention the weather.

Matter-of-fact.

Her eyes return to her work.

“You belong to coin now.”

She reaches for a small knife and begins slicing thin roots into the mixture.

Tap. Tap. Tap.

“You should eat.”

She pushes a wooden bowl across the floor toward you with her foot.

Inside is a thin stew. Mushrooms. Bitter herbs. Something stringy that might be meat.

It smells… edible.

The witch rises and begins hanging bundles of herbs over the fire.

The hut is quiet except for the fire popping and the soft chime of bones hanging by the doorway.

Night deepens outside.

Hours pass.

Eventually the witch begins preparing something more serious.

She clears a space in the center of the hut.

Chalk symbols appear on the floor.

Candles are placed carefully around a circle.

A small iron brazier begins burning with green flame.

Then she looks at you.

Her eyes glint in the firelight.

“Come here.”

Her voice is calm.

Too calm.

What do you do?
Eat the stew quietly and then approach the circle when she calls.
Refuse to move, staying by the hearth and watching her carefully.
Ask what she is doing with the circle and candles.
Pretend to cooperate while secretly watching for a chance to escape.
Knock over the bowl or candles and try to disrupt whatever she is preparing.

The stew is thin.

Watery mushrooms. Bitter roots. Something fibrous that might once have been meat. It doesn’t matter. Your stomach twists painfully as you eat. Every swallow burns down your throat like relief.

The witch doesn’t watch you.

She works.

Chalk scrapes across the floor. Candles are set. Powder is poured into the brazier. Green flames lick upward, casting strange shadows that crawl along the walls.

By the time the bowl is empty, your belly feels warm and heavy.

You stand slowly and walk toward her.

Your claws click softly against the packed dirt floor.

She glances down as you step into the chalk circle.

“Good.”

Her voice carries quiet satisfaction.

The candles are lit one by one.

Wax drips.

The air thickens with incense. Sharp. Bitter. Metallic.

The witch begins to speak.

Not in the trader’s tongue.

The words curl and twist like smoke. Ancient sounds that scrape against the inside of your skull.

Something changes.

The green flame flares brighter.

Your limbs grow heavy.

Very heavy.

Your thoughts slow… like they’re sinking into thick mud.

The witch kneels beside you.

Her hand presses gently to your forehead.

“Still now, little scale.”

Your body won’t move.

Your eyes can still see.

The knife flashes once in the green light.

Pain comes sharp and sudden—

Then distant.

Like it’s happening somewhere far away.

The world begins to dim.

You hear the witch working.

Metal tools clink softly.

The smell of blood mixes with incense.

Your body is used carefully, piece by piece, like ingredients laid out on a table. Nothing wasted. Nothing hurried.

Time becomes strange.

You feel… less.

Less weight. Less pain. Less breath.

At some point the world goes completely dark.

Then—

Awareness returns.

Not to breath.

Not to flesh.

To stillness.

A dim green glow filters through something translucent.

Your thoughts are slow at first… drifting… confused…

You are aware of the hut again.

The fire crackling.

The witch moving about the room.

But your body is gone.

Your vision comes from somewhere small.

Hanging.

Swinging slightly.

The witch sits at her workbench, carving runes into a small gem set inside a hanging bauble — polished bone wrapped with copper wire.

Inside the gem, faint green light pulses.

You feel it.

A tug.

A strange thread tying you to the object.

Your skull rests on a shelf nearby among other bones.

But you are not in it.

You are here.

In the gem.

The witch lifts the bauble, holding it up to the candlelight.

Her lips curl into a satisfied smile.

“Yes…”

She turns it slowly.

“Good anchor.”

She ties it to a cord hanging from her staff.

You swing gently as she stands.

For a moment, your awareness dims slightly — as if the magic binding you settles into place.

But when it clears…

You are still here.

Still aware.

Still watching.

Still thinking.

Your body is gone.

But you remain.

The witch hangs her staff beside the door.

You sway slightly from the motion.

The hut grows quiet.

Outside, rain taps against the roof.

Time begins to move again.

What do you focus on?

Try to move the bauble, testing if you can influence it at all.
Focus on the witch, studying her habits and movements.
Focus on the magic binding you, trying to understand the anchor and the gem.
Look toward your skull on the shelf, feeling that strange lingering connection.
Simply observe the hut and wait, learning about this new existence.

The forest is wet and quiet.

Branches scrape against the witch’s staff as she walks the narrow trail between the trees. Each step makes the bauble sway gently, the copper rings clicking faintly together.

You do not breathe.

You do not blink.

But you watch.

And you think.

At first the world is confusing — too many sensations without the body that once helped you understand them. There is no heartbeat. No breath. No muscles to tense.

But the gem gives you position. A place to exist.

You begin to understand one simple truth:

You are wherever the gem is.

Learning

The witch walks deep into the woods and eventually returns to the hut. She locks the door with a crooked iron latch and hangs the staff on a hook beside the doorway.

Then she eats.

The hut grows quiet.

The fire dies down to embers.

Outside, wind whispers through the trees.

Carefully.

Over the next nights…

Every time the witch sleeps.

You learn the limits.

• You cannot leave the gem.
• The farther you push from it, the stronger the magic pulls you back.
• The gem is the center of you now.

The anchor.

You do not know the word for it.

But you understand the idea.

If the gem is broken…

The thought makes your awareness recoil.

The Skull

One night, while the witch is asleep, your attention drifts across the room.

To the shelf.

You cannot reach it.

A distant tether.

Perhaps something else.

You do not know.

The Witch

Always.

She draws a small pouch from her belt and pours a pinch of dark powder into the water. The current carries it around the staff like smoke dissolving in glass.

Not loudly.

But the language of magic again.

Those twisting words you heard the night she killed you.

You watch closely.

This time you focus on the structure.

The spell begins in three places:

The Witch – her voice shaping the command.
The Staff – acting as the channel.
The Gem – where the energy is drawn from.

You feel it clearly.

Something inside you is pulled.

A thread of power leaving the gem.

Leaving you.

It flows into the staff.

Then out into the river.

The water begins to shimmer faintly.

The rider’s horse shifts nervously.

“What are you doing?” he asks.

“Watch.”

The witch lifts the staff slowly.

Water rises with it.

Not much.

Just a thin twisting column around the wood.

The rider leans forward in his saddle.

The witch speaks the final word of the spell.

The water drops back into the river.

But something remains.

A faint blue symbol burns briefly on the rider’s chest.

Then fades into his cloak.

The man blinks.

“What was that?”

“A ward,” the witch says calmly.

“For the next three nights, blades meant to harm you will slip. Arrows will stray. Ill fortune will look elsewhere.”

The rider hesitates.

“Convenient claim.”

“Try it if you like.”

He considers.

Finally he sighs and reaches into his belt pouch.

A small handful of coins drops into the witch’s waiting palm.

“Three nights,” he says.

“Three nights.”

The witch nods.

The rider turns his horse and rides off down the road.

Soon the sound of hooves fades into the forest.

The witch watches him go.

Then she chuckles softly.

“People will pay anything for a little luck.”

She taps the staff on the ground once.

You feel the gem settle again.

The pull on your essence stops.

But you learned something important.

The magic did not consume you.

It drew from you.

Like dipping a cup into a river.

If she does it too often…

If she draws too deeply…

Something inside the gem might eventually run dry.

And that something is you.

The witch turns back toward the forest trail.

“Productive morning.”

She begins walking.

The bauble sways as you move through the trees again.

What do you focus on now?
Study the spell you just witnessed, trying to understand how the power flowed.
Examine the gem internally, seeing how much of you was actually drained.
Observe the witch even more closely, looking for habits or weaknesses.
Extend your awareness into the forest, mapping the world around you.
Think about the skull again, wondering if distance affects that connection.

The witch walks deeper into the forest.

Branches brush the staff. The bauble sways gently beneath it. Sunlight flickers through leaves overhead, flashing across the gem again and again.

You turn your awareness inward.

Into the gem.

Into your prison.

At first there is nothing to see.

No color. No walls. No shape.

But there is a feeling.

You begin to understand that the gem holds you the way a vessel holds water.

Your consciousness is not a solid thing inside it — it’s more like a pool of energy shaped like your mind.

When the witch casts magic, she dips into that pool.

You replay the feeling from the river crossing.

You remember the moment the spell began.

The pull.

You examine it carefully.

It did not take a large piece.

Not even a painful piece.

More like someone drawing a cup from a lake.

You still feel whole.

Still aware.

Still you.

But the pool did shrink slightly.

Just a little.

Then something surprising happens.

Slowly…

Very slowly…

The pool refills.

Not from the witch.

Not from the gem itself.

From somewhere outside.

The world.

The air.

The living things around you.

Tiny threads of loose magic drift through the world constantly — the background hum of a magical land.

The gem gathers those threads.

And feeds them back into the pool.

Into you.

You realize something important.

The gem is not just a container.

It is a collector.

A slow one.

But steady.

If the witch draws power slowly, the pool will replenish.

If she draws too much too quickly…

The pool could empty.

And what happens then…

You cannot tell.

The thought chills you in a way that has nothing to do with temperature.

You examine the process further.

And you notice something subtle.

When the witch casts spells…

You have no control over the draw.

But inside the gem, your awareness can move through the pool.

The energy flows through channels — shaped by the runes carved into the gem and the wires binding it.

You cannot block them.

But you can feel them.

Like currents in water.

And maybe…

Just maybe…

Currents can be redirected.

Not stopped.

But guided.

You do not yet know how.

But the possibility exists.

Then another idea forms.

The pool grows slowly because the gem gathers loose magic from the world.

But your mind might also influence it.

If you learn to shape the energy inside the gem…

You might be able to:

• Store more before the witch draws it
• Slow the drain when she casts
• Redirect the flow through different channels

Not enough to break free.

Not yet.

But enough to survive longer.

The witch continues walking through the forest trail, unaware of the small intelligence studying the magic in her staff.

You hang beneath it.

Silent.

Learning.

Growing.

Practice shaping the energy pool, trying to make it store more magic.

Do nothing for now, simply letting the pool refill while observing more of the world.

You do nothing.

No pushing. No testing. No stirring the magic.

Just watching.

The Land

The forest around you slowly becomes familiar.

Tall old pines dominate the higher ground, their trunks straight and dark with age. Beneath them grow thick patches of ferns and moss. Fallen logs rot slowly into the earth, covered in pale mushrooms.

Lower ground near the river holds different trees — birch and alder, their white bark peeling like old skin.

You begin to recognize patterns in the terrain as the witch walks.

She follows certain paths repeatedly.

Narrow animal trails.

Old footpaths.

Once you pass a broken stone marker half-buried in moss — a relic from a road long abandoned.

You begin mapping the world quietly in your mind.

The hut lies somewhere deeper in the forest.

The road you saw earlier runs north and south.

Travelers occasionally pass it.

This means people exist nearby.

Villages.

Markets.

Possibly even towns.

The Witch’s Routine

You watch her habits carefully.

She travels far during the day.

Sometimes she gathers herbs.

Sometimes she meets travelers.

Sometimes she visits strange places.

Once she stops near a dead oak where dozens of bones hang from branches like wind chimes. She whispers something there, leaving a small bundle tied to the tree.

Some sort of offering.

Or communication.

You begin to realize she is part of something larger — not just a lone hermit.

Other forces exist in the forest.

The Magic

While she walks, you feel the gem quietly refilling.

Threads of ambient magic drift through the forest constantly.

The gem collects them like dew forming on glass.

The pool within you slowly grows deeper again.

The witch does not notice.

She likely expects this.

It is how her tool works.

But she does not realize the mind inside the battery is learning.

Hours Later

The witch returns toward the hut.

The sun is dropping behind the treetops.

Long shadows stretch across the forest floor.

As she walks, she begins humming again — the same tune you heard the night she killed you.

The melody is strange.

Almost like a lullaby.

When the hut finally appears through the trees, you recognize the area immediately.

Your prison.

The crooked roof.

The bone charms hanging in the doorway.

Smoke drifting from the chimney.

She pushes the door open and steps inside.

The staff is placed on its hook again.

You sway slightly as the gem settles.

The hut grows dim as dusk settles outside.

The witch begins preparing food.

Another quiet night is coming.

Another night where she sleeps.

Another night where you can practice unseen.

• Where the road is.
• That travelers pass nearby.
• That the forest has paths and landmarks.
• That the gem replenishes slowly over time.

You are still trapped.

But you are no longer blind.

Night approaches again.

Into the staff itself.

The staff is not just a stick.

It is conditioned.

Like a riverbed worn smooth by water.

Magic has traveled through it for many years.

The Structure

As your awareness moves deeper, you begin to sense its design.

The staff is layered with enchantments.

Not one spell.

Many.

Some are simple:

• reinforcement runes strengthening the wood
• minor conduits guiding magical flow
• bindings connecting the gem to the core of the staff

A framework.

A lattice of magical pathways that all converge on the gem.

From the gem.

From you.

The staff is a tool of direction.

You are the source.

Something Interesting

You follow one of the channels slowly.

It runs from the gem upward along the center of the staff… then splits into several branches.

Each branch corresponds to different types of magic the witch uses.

One channel smells of water magic — like the spell she cast earlier at the river.

Another feels sharp and hot — perhaps fire.

Another feels cold and still.

You realize something subtle.

The staff is not just a pipe.

It is more like a network of valves.

When the witch casts a spell, she opens one of these channels with her words and gestures.

Power flows through that path.

The rest remain closed.

You cannot control the channels.

Not yet.

But you can feel them before they open.

The moment the witch begins casting a spell…

You will know which pathway she is about to use.

That means you will feel the drain coming before it happens.

That knowledge might someday matter.

Deeper Still

Curiosity pulls you farther inward.

Near the very center of the staff’s enchantment…

You find something surprising.

A limit.

The staff itself cannot draw unlimited power.

The enchantment includes safeguards.

If too much energy flows at once, the channels begin to fracture.

The wood would split.

The magic would collapse.

The witch knows this.

Which is why she draws slowly.

Carefully.

Always measured.

At the base of the staff…

Where the gem is mounted…

You notice a small but important detail.

The binding runes connecting the gem to the staff are not perfectly symmetrical.

One of them has been repaired.

Recently.

The rune line there is slightly weaker.

A patch.

The witch likely fixed damage there sometime in the past.

It still works.

But it is the weakest point in the whole structure.

You do not touch it.

You do not push.

You only remember.

The hut remains quiet.

The staff leans against the wall.

The Binding

You find the runes again.

They are carved directly into the metal clasp holding the gem to the staff. Thin copper bands circle the stone, each etched with tiny symbols no wider than a claw-tip.

At first glance they seem chaotic.

But as your awareness studies them, a pattern begins to reveal itself.

There are four primary binding runes.

Each serves a different purpose.

You slowly map them.

Rune One — Containment

This rune anchors the soul inside the gem.

You feel its grip constantly.

It is the leash.

The prison wall.

It defines the boundary of your existence.

Without it… the soul inside the gem would disperse.

Or escape.

You do not know which.

Rune Two — Stabilization

This rune prevents the soul-energy from tearing the gem apart.

Souls are not meant to be bottled.

Without stabilization, the energy would crack the stone over time.

This rune keeps the structure intact.

You feel it working constantly.

Quietly.

Like bones supporting flesh.

Rune Three — Conduit

This one connects the gem to the staff’s magical channels.

It is the tap the witch uses.

When she casts spells, this rune opens and allows power to flow upward into the staff.

This rune is why the staff can drain you.

Rune Four — Control

This is the witch’s leash.

It prevents the soul inside the gem from resisting the drain.

It keeps the energy passive.

Obedient.

Tool-like.

The Damaged Rune

Now you examine the weak spot.

The repair.

It lies along the conduit rune.

At some point in the past, the channel cracked — perhaps from drawing too much power at once.

The witch repaired it carefully.

But the line is not perfect.

Where the rune was mended, the magic flows slightly unevenly.

You can feel the current swirl there.

Not breaking.

But unstable.

Like water flowing over a cracked stone.

A Possibility

If the conduit rune weakened further…

The staff might struggle to draw power from the gem.

Not stop completely.

But become less efficient.

The witch might think the gem was simply running low.

Or aging.

She might not suspect a mind inside it.

But the risk is obvious.

If the rune breaks completely…

The staff could lose control of the energy.

The backlash might damage the gem.

And if the gem breaks…

You do not know what happens to you.

The containment rune and the control rune overlap slightly.

The control rune suppresses the soul’s ability to resist.

But it does not completely erase it.

That suppression works best when the soul inside the gem remains passive.

Unaware.

Inactive.

You are thinking.

Learning.

Exploring.

Moments where the control rune strains slightly to hold you quiet.

The witch never expected the soul inside the gem to wake up.

The witch designed the rune expecting a trapped soul to thrash.

The Second Ring

The first ring holds.

Studying the Structure

You stop occasionally.

You notice something important.

The outer layers of the pool swirl in wide, lazy loops.

But deeper layers move differently.

Sharper.

Faster.

More focused.

The currents here behave less like water… and more like threads pulled tight across a loom.

This is where the witch’s magic pulls from when she needs stronger spells.

Your reservoir must protect against that.

The next layer cannot simply redirect flow.

It must cut through it.

Hold shape against pressure.

You begin to understand why the original containment rune uses sharp angles and intersecting lines.

Soft curves guide currents.

i go for one of the clearest and sharpest memories.. the one of his sacrifice.. the moment the knife fell

The hut sleeps.

The witch breathes slowly in the darkness, one arm hanging from the bed. The fire has collapsed into dull embers that glow like watchful eyes.

The staff leans beside the door.

The gem is still.

Inside it…

You turn toward the skull again.

The Memory

You reach for the sharpest moment.

The one you have avoided until now.

The moment when the knife fell.

At first the skull resists.

Not because the memory is gone…

…but because it is heavy.

When you finally touch it, the world snaps into place with terrible clarity.

You stand again inside the chalk circle.

The hut smells of incense and blood.

The witch’s voice murmurs strange words above you.

Your limbs are heavy.

You cannot move.

You remember the exact feeling of your heart beating in your chest.

Fast.

Hard.

Trying to escape.

You remember the green light reflecting in the blade.

You remember knowing—completely, absolutely—that the next moment would be the last.

Then the knife moved.

The memory freezes there.

That instant.

The precise moment when awareness became a single point.

No fear.

No confusion.

Just perfect clarity.

Inside the Gem

The effect is immediate.

The energy pool tightens.

Where peaceful memories created smooth currents…

This memory creates edges.

Clean.

Sharp.

Stable.

You shape the first line of the third structure.

Not a curve.

A point.

It cuts through the currents like the blade that created the memory.

The energy around it parts cleanly.

No turbulence.

No drift.

It holds.

You add another line.

Then another.

The structure begins forming deep inside the second ring.

An angular lattice.

Small.

Precise.

Every intersection anchored by that frozen moment of awareness.

The moment before death.

The Result

The pool reacts in a way you did not expect.

Where the outer rings guide energy…

This inner structure locks it.

Currents entering the third layer slow dramatically.

Pressure builds slightly outside it.

Inside, the energy remains almost perfectly still.

Your hidden reservoir has gained its first true barrier.

Not impenetrable.

But strong.

Much stronger than the earlier rings.

Across the room the witch shifts in her sleep.

You stop instantly.

Everything settles.

The currents return to their normal flow.

The sharp structure remains hidden beneath the surface.

She snores softly.

Still unaware.

Something Changes

When you return your attention inward, you notice something new.

Your awareness feels…

Clearer.

More focused.

The memory you used has done more than anchor the structure.

It has sharpened you.

The control rune still presses down on your will…

…but the pressure feels slightly weaker when you focus through the lattice.

As if the sharp structure gives your mind a place to stand against it.

You cannot resist the rune.

Not yet.

But you can think more clearly beneath it.

Outside the hut, the wind moves through the forest.

Somewhere in the distance an owl calls.

Inside the gem, the first lines of your deepest defense now exist.

The blade that killed you has become the foundation of your survival.

Night continues.

You could continue shaping the third structure…

…but the memory you used carries weight.

Holding it too long may disturb the gem’s balance.

What do you do next?
Continue carefully shaping the third layer, building more of the sharp lattice.
Release the memory and let the structure settle, avoiding suspicion tonight.
Study how the new lattice affects the control rune, testing your clearer awareness.
Examine the conduit rune again, seeing how the deeper structure alters energy flow.
Reach outward to the skull again, searching for another sharp memory to reinforce the lattice.
i release it.. letting it settle.. i know i will need to revisit it again and again to build it properly.. but cant let it become obsessive.. so i revisit the outer rings and their memories to help settle the sharpness of the third

The memory releases slowly.

You let the moment fade before it becomes a wound that consumes everything else. The blade. The green light. The final stillness. You allow it to drift back into the skull where it belongs.

Inside the gem, the sharp lattice you began remains.

Small.

Precise.

A few intersecting angles deep within the second ring.

It no longer presses against the rest of your awareness. Instead it sits there like the tip of a spear buried beneath layers of calm water.

Stable.

Hidden.

Settling the Structure

You turn your attention outward again—not outside the gem, but to the wider pool.

To the first ring.

You revisit the memory that holds it.

The trader’s wagon creaking along muddy roads. The rope biting your wrists. The smell of wet leather and horse sweat. The slow, miserable certainty that you were being carried toward something terrible.

Those memories are heavy.

But they are broad memories.

They anchor the outer ring firmly.

You allow those currents to flow again.

The sharp pressure from the inner lattice softens slightly as the outer ring takes the strain.

Like a fortress wall absorbing the wind around a needle-sharp tower.

Then you move deeper.

To the second ring.

The calm memories.

The tunnels.

The warmth of packed earth beneath your claws.

The quiet murmur of your clutchmates.

The steady rhythm of digging.

These memories smooth the currents beautifully.

The energy pool calms again.

The sharp lattice inside the third layer remains, but it no longer dominates the structure.

Now the three layers behave like a living system:

• Outer Ring — strength born from suffering and endurance.
• Second Ring — calm guidance, smooth flow.
• Third Lattice — precise, immovable focus.

Each balances the others.

None draws too much attention from the gem’s natural circulation.

A Subtle Effect

As the currents settle, you notice something interesting.

The energy inside the gem now organizes itself more efficiently than before.

Instead of drifting randomly, the currents move through the rings in layered circulation.

The gem refills from ambient magic as it always has…

…but now that energy distributes itself more evenly.

Slowly.

Quietly.

Your reservoir grows deeper.

Still hidden.

Still natural-looking to the runes.

The witch would see nothing unusual.

Only a well-behaved focus gem doing exactly what it was designed to do.

The Witch Sleeps

Across the room she shifts again.

One eye opens briefly.

You still every current.

The gem glows faint green.

Unchanged.

Her eye closes again.

A low snore follows.

The hut returns to silence.

You remain still for the rest of the night.

Not building.

Just letting the structures become part of the gem.

Letting the magic accept them as natural.

Letting suspicion fade.

Before Dawn

When the grey light begins to creep through the hut’s walls again, your three layers remain intact.

Hidden.

Balanced.

Patient.

The witch wakes, stretches, and glances at the gem like she does every morning.

Her eyes linger only a moment.

Then she nods to herself.

“Still strong.”

She takes the staff and begins preparing for another day.

Inside the gem, your quiet architecture holds.

You have time.

And you are learning patience.

As the new day begins, what do you focus on?
Watch travelers again, gathering more knowledge about the wider world and the tower rumors.
Observe the witch’s spellcasting closely, studying how the energy flows through your new layered reservoir.
Study the bone hill more carefully next visit, exploring the faint connections to the rest of your body.
Examine the control rune again, now that your inner lattice sharpens your awareness.
Map the forest more precisely, building a full mental map of the witch’s territory.
i observe the world as she travels.. listening to the travels as the come to her.. watch her magic closely when she uses it, and listens closely to the bones to hear their whispers

Days pass into weeks.

You remain silent inside the gem, letting the witch believe exactly what she believes: that the green stone holds nothing but a docile soul-battery.

Meanwhile, you watch.

You listen.

And the world slowly grows larger around you.

The Roads and the World Beyond

Travelers come and go at the river crossing.

Not every day, but often enough that the road is never completely silent for long.

You begin to recognize patterns in people.

Merchants ride heavy wagons and complain loudly.

Hunters travel light and watch the tree line.

Soldiers ride straight-backed and speak little.

From them you gather pieces of the world.

Sometimes the conversations are trivial:

Prices rising in Velkarr Crossing.
Road tolls near Ironford.
A caravan delayed by floods.

But other times…

The news is sharper.

One afternoon two riders stop to water their horses.

One says quietly:

“Redstone Ridge is closing the north road.”

The other spits into the river.

“Because of the tower?”

“Aye.”

“What did they see?”

“Lights in the upper windows. And something walking the walls.”

The witch pretends not to listen.

But you feel her grip tighten slightly on the staff.

You listen harder.

The first rider continues:

“They sent men to investigate last winter. None came back.”

The second rider curses softly.

“Should’ve burned the place years ago.”

They leave soon after.

But the witch remains silent for a long time.

The idea has clearly taken root in her mind.

Watching the Witch’s Magic

You study every spell she casts.

Now that your reservoir has structure, the energy behaves differently when she draws from it.

When the conduit rune opens, the currents respond in layers.

The outer pool moves first.

The second ring redirects flow smoothly.

When she draws harder—fire spells or heavier charms—the pressure pushes deeper…

…until the flow meets the sharp lattice.

And there the current slows sharply.

The draw becomes less efficient.

Not enough for her to notice.

But enough that your hidden core remains untouched.

Your plan is working.

The Bone Hill

You listen more carefully each time she visits the hill.

The bones whisper in ways that are not quite sound.

More like pressure in the magic.

When she scatters powder and speaks to the trees, the bone-magic channel opens again.

The bones respond.

But not individually.

Something in the forest answers through them.

The bones are like a row of hollow pipes carrying wind.

You begin to sense patterns in the responses.

Not words.

But meanings.

Sometimes approval.

Sometimes warning.

Once…

Something like irritation.

The witch only laughs at that.

“Old things grow cranky with age.”

The fragments of your body react faintly during these exchanges.

The rib.

The femur.

The half-buried pelvis.

Each gives the slightest tug in your awareness.

They remember shape, not thought.

But the connection exists.

Small threads linking your old body to the soul inside the gem.

Too weak to control.

But not meaningless.

The Witch’s Curiosity

Her attention keeps drifting north now.

Toward the mountains.

Toward the place the riders mentioned.

One evening while stirring herbs over the fire she mutters quietly:

“If the tower truly wakes…”

She taps the staff against the floor.

“…there may be things worth finding there.”

Your gem sways slightly as she shifts.

Your awareness sharpens.

A journey may be coming.

A longer one than her usual paths.

Inside the Gem

Your structures remain stable.

The rings circulate quietly.

The sharp lattice holds.

Every day the gem gathers more ambient magic from the forest.

Your reservoir deepens.

Your mind grows clearer.

The control rune still suppresses resistance…

…but it struggles slightly against the precision of your inner structure.

The witch cannot feel it.

Yet.

Night will come again soon.

Another opportunity for quiet work.

But something else is approaching as well.

The witch’s curiosity about the tower grows stronger.

And if she travels there…

You will see more of the world than ever before.

When night falls again, what do you focus on?
Continue expanding the third lattice, strengthening the core of your reservoir.
Study the control rune again, now that your mind is sharper against it.
Experiment with the faint connections to your scattered bones, testing their limits.
Analyze the bone-magic conversation more deeply, trying to understand the forest entity.
Examine the repaired conduit fracture again, considering whether it could someday be exploited.
i continue the third latice, and prepare for the fourth and final layer.. the bedrock for it all.. and for that he goes back to his earliest memories.. some of the best.. fresh hatched. in his motehrs arms.. playing with siblings in his childhood.. innocents

Night comes quietly.

The witch sleeps.

The staff rests where it always does, leaning beside the door, your bauble hanging beneath it like a dull green star.

The hut breathes.

And inside the gem, you return to your work.

The Third Lattice

You revisit the sharp structure you began.

The memory of the knife.

The moment when everything became a single point of awareness.

You do not hold the memory long this time—only enough to sharpen each line.

One angle at a time.

Each intersection locks against the next like bone joints fitted perfectly together.

The lattice grows.

Not large.

But dense.

A small cage of precision deep within the second ring.

The currents of magic now move through the gem in four distinct behaviors:

• Outer flow – slow, broad, natural.
• Second ring – guided circulation.
• Third lattice – controlled pressure.
• The core… still empty.

That emptiness is what you now prepare.

The Fourth Layer

You know what it must be.

Not strength.

Not calm.

Not focus.

Those already exist.

The final layer must be foundation.

Something deeper than fear or clarity.

Something that does not shift even when everything else changes.

For that, you return to the skull again.

But you do not search for pain.

Or danger.

You go deeper.

Farther back.

To the earliest marks life left inside bone.

The First Memories

At first the skull offers nothing.

Just faint echoes.

Then slowly…

Warmth.

You feel soft scales against your skin.

A body larger than yours curled protectively around you.

Your mother.

The memory is blurry, but the feeling is unmistakable.

Safety.

You remember the sound of her breathing.

Slow and deep.

Your tiny claws gripping her scales as you slept.

Inside the gem, the currents settle.

Not just calm.

Still.

Another memory rises.

You are small—barely able to walk straight.

Your clutchmates tumble over each other in the dirt of the nursery tunnel.

Someone squeaks with triumph after stealing a beetle.

You chase them.

You fall.

Everyone piles into a laughing knot of scales and tails.

No fear.

No hunger.

Just life beginning.

These memories behave differently from all the others.

They do not anchor shapes.

They anchor being.

Your awareness itself becomes steadier.

The control rune presses down on your will…

…but the foundation beneath you does not move.

The Bedrock

You begin shaping the final structure.

Not a ring.

Not a lattice.

A core.

A quiet, dense knot at the very center of the gem.

The earliest memory of your existence holds it steady.

Your mother’s warmth.

Your siblings’ laughter.

The feeling of simply being alive.

These memories are not sharp like the knife.

They are not strong like the trader’s cruelty.

They are immovable.

And so the core forms slowly.

A stable heart beneath the lattice.

Beneath the rings.

A place where the currents cannot easily reach.

The Result

When the structure settles, the entire pool changes.

The currents now flow in layers like a deep well:

Outer currents feeding the staff.
Guided flow through the second ring.
Pressure caught by the lattice.
And at the very bottom…

A still, silent reservoir.

Your true self.

Hidden.

Protected.

Almost unreachable.

Across the room, the witch stirs.

You stop instantly.

Everything stills.

The gem glows faintly as it always has.

Nothing unusual.

She rolls over and snores softly again.

Inside the gem, the architecture of your survival now stands nearly complete.

Four layers.

Strength.

Calm.

Precision.

And foundation.

A prison… quietly reshaped from within.

Outside, the wind moves through the forest.

Somewhere far to the north, the ruined tower burns faint lights in its upper windows.

And the witch’s curiosity about it continues to grow.

What do you focus on next?
Refining the fourth core, ensuring it remains completely hidden from the conduit rune.
Testing how spells draw energy now, observing the new layered flow carefully.
Studying the control rune again, seeing how your strengthened mind presses against it.
Exploring the faint links to the rest of your bones, testing whether the new core strengthens them.
Listening more carefully to the bone hill whispers, trying to understand the forest entity.
i spend the rest of the night refining the core in preperation for tommorow.. tommorow he will observe how the magic reacts, how the witch notices

The witch sleeps.

Outside, the forest holds its breath under a thin blanket of mist. Somewhere in the distance an owl calls once… then again.

Inside the hut, nothing moves.

The staff rests against the wall.

The bauble hangs.

And deep within it…

You work.

Refining the Core

You return to the earliest memory again.

Not forcing it.

Letting it exist.

Your mother’s warmth. The slow rhythm of her breathing. The dim light of fungus glowing along the nursery tunnel walls.

You remember how the world felt when you were newly hatched.

No fear.

No hunger yet.

Just being.

That memory does not create edges like the knife memory.

It does not create currents like the tunnel memories.

Instead it stills everything.

Inside the gem, the core you shaped becomes denser.

Not larger.

Just more real.

The currents of magic flowing through the gem move around it naturally, as if the core had always been there.

The Architecture

You examine the whole structure carefully.

Four layers now exist:

Outer Pool
The visible energy the witch draws from. It flows normally through the conduit rune.

First Ring – Endurance
The trader’s journey. Hard roads. Pain endured.

Second Ring – Calm Guidance
Tunnel life. Steady work. Quiet rhythm.

Third Lattice – Precision
The moment before the blade. Focus sharper than fear.

Fourth Core – Foundation
The earliest memory. The beginning of you.

You spend hours making tiny adjustments.

Not changing the shapes.

Just smoothing the way the currents pass between them.

Like a mason polishing the stones of a hidden foundation.

Every adjustment becomes smaller.

Subtler.

Until finally the gem’s internal flow looks… natural again.

Even to your heightened awareness.

If the witch notices anything tomorrow…

It will not be obvious.

A Subtle Discovery

While refining the core, you notice something unexpected.

The control rune presses against your will as it always has.

But the pressure does not reach the core.

The outer layers feel it.

The rings.

Even the lattice.

But the foundation beneath them remains untouched.

Not free.

But untouched.

Your true self now sits below the reach of the leash.

You cannot break it yet.

But you have created somewhere the rune cannot easily reach.

The Night Ends

You withdraw slowly as the night begins to pale.

The witch shifts in her bed.

The hut creaks softly as the wind changes.

The structures inside the gem settle into stillness.

Your work is finished for tonight.

Now comes the test.

Morning

Grey light creeps through the cracks in the hut walls.

The witch wakes slowly.

She sits up, rubs her eyes, and looks toward the staff.

Toward the gem.

Toward you.

Your awareness remains perfectly still.

The currents move as they should.

Nothing strained.

Nothing blocked.

Just a quiet green glow.

She squints slightly.

Then stands and walks over.

Her fingers close around the bauble.

For several long moments she studies it in the morning light.

Your structures remain hidden beneath the surface flow.

Finally she nods.

“Mmm.”

She hangs the staff back on the hook and begins preparing the fire.

No alarm.

No suspicion.

But the real test will come later.

When she uses magic.

When the conduit rune opens and the draw begins.

Then you will see how your hidden architecture truly behaves.

The day begins.

Soon she will leave the hut again.

What do you watch for most carefully today?
The first spell she casts, studying exactly how the draw interacts with your layers.
Her reaction to the gem, watching for any subtle suspicion.
The bone hill again, to see if the forest entity reacts to the change.
Travelers on the road, listening for more news about the Tower.
The ambient magic refilling the gem, measuring how your reservoir behaves now.
i watch her activities as normal.. the people, her travels.. but watch slosely when she cast spells, see how the magic behaves, and how it refills

Morning unfolds like every other.

The witch rekindles the fire, drinks her bitter herb broth, and gathers her satchel. The staff comes down from its hook, and the gem swings beneath it as she steps out into the forest.

You remain silent.

Watching.

Measuring.

Waiting.

Today is a test.

The First Spell

It happens near the river crossing.

A hunter approaches—young, nervous, carrying a cracked bow. He speaks quickly, glancing over his shoulder as if something might be following him.

The witch listens.

Nods.

He pays with a handful of copper.

Then she plants the staff into the earth.

You feel the conduit rune open.

This is the moment.

The Draw

Energy begins to move.

The outer pool responds first, exactly as before.

A broad current flows upward into the staff’s channel.

The hunter’s charm spell is minor—protection against bad luck in the forest.

The flow reaches the first ring.

Your trader-road memories hold firm. The current bends smoothly around the ring without resistance.

Good.

Then pressure increases slightly.

The draw deepens.

Energy reaches the second ring.

The calm tunnel memories guide the current in a wide circulation pattern, feeding the conduit without turbulence.

Still perfect.

Then, for a brief moment, the current presses toward the third lattice.

Here the change is obvious to you.

The sharp structure compresses the flow.

Not stopping it.

Just narrowing it.

Like water forced through a narrow stone channel.

The draw becomes slightly less efficient.

But the outer layers still provide enough power for the spell.

The witch notices nothing.

The charm completes.

A faint glow flickers on the hunter’s bow.

He thanks her and leaves.

The Core

The most important moment comes after.

When the pressure drops.

The conduit rune closes.

The energy currents settle.

And the flow never touches the core.

Not even slightly.

Your foundation remains perfectly still.

Untouched.

Hidden beneath every other layer.

Your true self is safe.

Refilling

You watch the next part carefully.

The gem begins pulling in ambient magic again.

The forest is full of it—faint threads drifting through soil, roots, water, and living creatures.

Before your work, the energy simply pooled randomly.

Now…

It follows paths.

The rings guide it.

The lattice stabilizes pressure.

The core quietly collects what slips past.

Refilling happens faster than before.

Not dramatically.

But enough that you notice.

The witch might eventually notice too if she measures carefully.

But for now, it simply appears that the gem is healthy.

Perhaps even unusually stable.

A valuable tool.

Later That Day

She casts two more spells.

A warding whisper at the bone hill.

And a minor heat charm while cooking.

Both draws behave exactly the same.

Outer layers feed the magic.

The lattice compresses deeper pressure.

The core remains untouched.

And every time the spell ends…

The gem refills.

Quietly.

Naturally.

The Witch

You watch her face carefully during every spell.

There is no suspicion.

No hesitation.

If anything…

She seems pleased.

One afternoon she even mutters while examining the gem:

“Good stone. Holding better than the last one.”

She has no idea why.

Night Returns

Back at the hut the witch finishes her supper and lies down again.

The staff returns to its hook.

The gem settles.

Inside it, your architecture stands firm.

Four layers deep.

Invisible.

Working exactly as you hoped.

But as the witch drifts toward sleep, she murmurs something that catches your attention.

Half-dreaming, she whispers:

“…the tower will need stronger magic.”

Her hand twitches toward the staff.

“…good thing this one is stable.”

If she goes to the tower…

She may draw far more power than usual.

Far more.

And that will test your work in ways you have not yet seen.

The witch sleeps again. What do you do tonight?
Strengthen the third lattice further, preparing for heavier magical draws.
Expand the hidden core slightly, increasing the protected reservoir.
Study the control rune again, testing how your deeper foundation resists it.
Experiment with the faint links to your scattered bones, seeing if your stronger core affects them.
Observe the witch’s dreams, hoping to glimpse the tower she plans to visit.

Night settles again over the hut.

The witch sleeps deeply tonight. Rain taps faintly against the roof, and the forest outside hums with insects and distant frogs. The staff leans in its usual place, and the gem hangs quiet and obedient.

Inside it, you begin the most careful study you have attempted yet.

Not of yourself.

Of the weapon that holds you.

The Staff’s Safeguards

You move your awareness up through the gem’s binding into the staff again.

The channels are clearer to you now than they were before.

When you first examined them, they seemed like simple conduits—paths the witch opened when she cast spells.

Now you see the deeper structure.

There are three protections built into the staff:

1 — Flow Limiters

Small regulating runes that prevent too much energy from being drawn at once.

If the witch attempts a spell beyond the gem’s safe capacity, these runes constrict the channel.

The draw slows.

The spell weakens.

The staff survives.

2 — Feedback Dampeners

These absorb excess magical pressure.

If energy surges through the channels too quickly, the dampeners redirect it into the wood of the staff itself.

The staff warms slightly, but the gem remains stable.

Without these dampeners, a surge could fracture the conduit rune.

3 — Emergency Grounding

The most important safeguard.

If the gem destabilizes entirely, the staff can vent the energy harmlessly into the earth through the base of the wood.

The power dissipates into the ground.

The gem survives.

The witch loses the spell—but not her tool.

The staff was built by someone experienced.

Someone who understood what happens when soul magic goes wrong.

The Weakness

You return to the damaged conduit rune—the repair you noticed weeks ago.

The patch still holds.

But the repair did not fully reconnect the original flow geometry.

It created a subtle imbalance.

Under normal use, the flow passes smoothly.

But if pressure rose rapidly…

That imbalance could destabilize the regulators.

And if the regulators fail…

The dampeners will attempt to absorb the surge.

If the dampeners overload…

Only the grounding rune remains.

But the grounding rune has one fatal flaw.

It depends on the staff being in contact with the ground.

If the grounding pathway is disrupted…

The energy has nowhere to go.

You see the chain clearly now.

Break the grounding path.
Destabilize the regulators.
Overload the dampeners.

And the staff will consume everything available to it.

A catastrophic draw.

It will try to drain the gem completely.

The Risk

If that happens now…

You would almost certainly vanish with the rest of the energy.

The gem would burn empty.

And your soul would go with it.

Unless…

The Countermeasure

You turn inward again.

Your four-layer structure is strong.

But a catastrophic draw would still tear through the outer layers.

You begin planning the reinforcement.

The key is timing and compression.

If the surge begins, the outer layers must collapse inward intentionally—feeding the staff just enough energy to appear normal—while sealing the inner core completely.

The lattice will need reinforcement.

Sharp angles.

Multiple pressure points.

A structure capable of absorbing violent currents without letting them reach the foundation.

You spend the rest of the night simulating the surge in your mind.

Imagining how the currents would move.

Where the pressure would strike first.

Where the rings would need strengthening.

Where the lattice must lock.

Where the core must seal.

The architecture becomes clearer.

A hidden fortress beneath a sacrificial outer shell.

Dawn

When the witch wakes, nothing has changed.

The gem glows softly.

Stable.

Healthy.

Valuable.

She lifts the staff and nods to herself.

“Still strong.”

If anything, she seems pleased with how reliable it has become.

She has no idea that the battery she carries is now quietly designing the weapon that could destroy her staff.

And somewhere far to the north…

The tower waits.

A place where the witch may attempt magic powerful enough to test everything you’ve built.

The day begins again.

What do you focus on now?

Reinforce the third lattice, preparing it to withstand a catastrophic surge.
Study the grounding rune more closely, determining how it could be disrupted at the right moment.
Observe the bone hill again, seeing if the forest entity reacts to your growing power.
Continue mapping the forest, preparing for the possibility of the witch traveling north.
Watch travelers carefully, hoping to learn more about the tower before the witch reaches it.

Morning mist clings low to the forest floor.

The witch walks her usual path, staff tapping softly against roots and stones. You sway beneath it, your awareness drifting through the small sphere around the gem as you watch the woods wake up.

Birds chatter. A fox slips across the trail ahead of her and vanishes into brush. The world continues its quiet rhythm.

Eventually, the land rises toward the place you know well now.

The Hill of Bones.

Dead trees stretch upward like black fingers. Wind whistles through their branches, making the hanging bones clatter softly together.

The witch steps into the clearing and plants her staff in the soil.

The bone-magic channel opens faintly.

You listen.

The Whispering

She scatters grey powder again at the base of the central tree.

“Old watchers,” she murmurs.

“Tell me what moves in these woods.”

The bones shift.

Not violently.

Just small movements against the wind.

You focus your awareness outward.

The magic here feels different from the staff’s magic.

Older.

Diffuse.

Like roots spreading through soil.

You feel the faint tug from your scattered bones again—your rib, the femur, the half-buried pelvis.

They are part of the chorus now.

Not voices.

But resonators.

Something in the forest speaks through them.

The witch tilts her head slightly.

Listening.

You try to follow the currents the way you’ve learned to follow the staff’s runes.

Something moves through the trees.

A pressure.

A presence that brushes past the bones and carries meaning.

Fragments of understanding reach you.

Movement on the road.
Men with knives.
Blood in the brush.

The witch nods slowly.

“Bandits again,” she says quietly.

The Intrusion

Not long after, the forest answers the warning.

Branches snap somewhere down the trail.

Heavy footsteps.

A man emerges from the brush.

Leather armor patched together poorly. A short sword at his hip. A crossbow slung across his back.

A bandit.

He freezes when he sees the witch.

Then he grins.

“Well now… what have we got here?”

The witch doesn’t move.

Her staff remains planted in the dirt.

Your gem sways gently.

The bandit steps closer.

Old habits of intimidation roll easily off his tongue.

“Nice staff. Fancy charms.”

He glances at the bones hanging in the trees.

“Bet you’ve got coin too, old woman.”

The witch says nothing.

Her eyes study him calmly.

The bandit steps closer still.

Too close.

His hand rests on the hilt of his sword.

“You deaf or just stupid?”

He reaches for the staff.

The Spell

The moment his fingers touch the wood—

The bone-magic channel flares open.

You feel the draw immediately.

But it is not pulling only from the gem.

The bones in the trees vibrate.

The rib that once belonged to you rattles against its cord.

The magic flows through everything here.

The witch speaks a single word.

Sharp.

Old.

The forest answers.

The bandit’s grin fades.

Something moves in the underbrush behind him.

Then another sound.

Then many.

Shadows shift beneath the trees.

Shapes step forward.

Wolves.

Three of them.

Silent.

Eyes fixed on the bandit.

The witch never even raises the staff.

She simply says calmly:

“You were warned.”

The bandit panics.

He fumbles for his sword.

But the wolves are already moving.

The forest erupts in snarling, snapping motion.

You do not see everything clearly through the chaos.

But the fight is short.

The bandit’s screams fade quickly.

The wolves drag what remains into the brush.

Silence returns.

The witch pulls the staff from the ground.

The bone-magic channel closes.

She looks around the clearing once more.

Then mutters softly:

“Good watchers.”

The bones sway gently.

Your rib bone clicks faintly against the branch.

For just a moment, you feel something brush your awareness through it.

Not speech.

But recognition.

A distant echo acknowledging the soul that once lived in that body.

Then the presence fades back into the forest.

The witch leaves the hill soon after.

The clearing returns to stillness.

But you have learned something new.

The bone hill is not merely a listening post.

It is part of a pact.

The witch feeds the forest.

And the forest watches for her.

The staff sways as she walks back toward the trail.

Another day continues.

Another piece of the world revealed.

What do you focus on next?
Study the bone-magic more deeply, trying to understand the pact between the witch and the forest.
Examine your connection to the rib and other bones, exploring whether they could become anchors like the skull.
Watch the witch’s reaction to the bandit’s death, learning how she handles danger.
Observe the wolves’ behavior, seeing if they were summoned or simply guided.
Return to studying the staff’s runes tonight, refining your sabotage plan.

The witch returns to the Hill of Bones two days later.

You feel the place before you see it.

The forest quiets here. Not silent—but attentive. The wind moves differently through the dead branches, and the bones hanging from cords shift with a dry clatter like teeth knocking together.

She plants the staff in the earth again.

Your gem sways.

The bone-magic channel opens.

Cold magic flows outward into the clearing.

You focus your awareness not on the forest this time—but on the bones themselves.

The Body That Was Yours

The skull remains the strongest anchor.

That much you already know.

But now you turn to the others.

The Rib

It hangs from a black thread about head height.

You reach toward it carefully.

There is a connection.

Faint… but present.

Not a mind.

Not even a memory.

What it holds is shape.

A structural echo of what your body once was.

When the witch’s magic passes through the bone hill, the rib vibrates like a tuning fork.

And you feel that vibration in your awareness.

It does not give you images or thoughts.

It gives you something stranger:

A sense of space.

The memory of breath expanding a chest.

The curve of your body bending as you crawled through tunnels.

The rib remembers movement.

The Femur

Further up the tree, the femur turns slowly in the wind.

You reach toward it.

The connection there is weaker.

But clearer in a different way.

This bone remembers strength.

Weight.

Balance.

The way muscles once pulled against it when you ran or climbed.

It carries echoes of force and motion.

You realize something important.

The skull remembers your mind.

But the rest of the bones remember your body.

The Pelvis

Half buried in the dirt near the roots.

You reach toward it last.

The connection is muddy here.

The bone is partially swallowed by soil and roots.

But it holds something deeper.

Center.

Balance.

The axis around which the rest of your body once moved.

Your awareness touches it only briefly before pulling back.

There is something heavy about that connection.

Old forest magic coils around bones buried in soil.

The witch’s pact runs strongest here.

The Communion

While you explore the bones, the witch whispers again.

“Watchers of root and branch.”

“Tell me what walks the northern roads.”

The forest answers.

You feel it move through the bones again like wind through hollow pipes.

This time, you pay close attention.

The bones do not create the magic.

They translate it.

Each bone carries a different resonance.

The skull transmits thought.

Ribs carry breath and movement.

Leg bones carry motion and strength.

Pelvis anchors the body.

Together, they form a crude echo of a living creature.

A body that the forest uses as a listening instrument.

Something Notices

For a moment—just a moment—you push a little deeper through the rib.

Not enough to move it.

Just enough to listen more closely.

And something in the forest pauses.

The pressure in the magic shifts.

Like a large animal lifting its head.

The wolves that sometimes answer the witch’s call are not what you feel.

This is older.

Slower.

Something that watches through roots and soil.

It does not understand what you are.

But it feels the shape of something familiar.

A body without flesh.

A soul without ground.

Then the witch speaks again.

The moment passes.

The forest’s attention drifts away.

What You Learn

As the bone-magic fades and the witch leaves the clearing, you understand something new.

Your body is not merely scattered remains.

It is still part of a network.

Each bone holds a piece of what you once were.

Individually they are weak.

But together…

They form something very close to a second anchor.

Not like the skull.

But something that could matter.

Especially if the staff were ever destroyed.

Especially if the gem were ever broken.

The witch leaves the hill again, unaware of your exploration.

The forest closes behind her.

The bones sway gently in the wind.

Your rib taps softly against the branch as she passes.

For just a moment…

It almost feels like your body remembers walking.

What do you focus on next?
Experiment with synchronizing the bones, seeing if their combined resonance strengthens your presence.
Study the forest presence more carefully next time, trying to understand what the witch calls the “watchers.”
Continue refining your hidden reservoir tonight, preparing for the tower’s heavy magic.
Analyze how your bones might act as a fallback anchor if the gem is ever destroyed.

Night settles over the hut once more.

The witch eats little tonight—just a cup of broth and a strip of dried meat. She stirs the fire, mutters a short ward into the embers, and crawls into her bed.

The staff returns to its hook.

You hang in the dim light.

Waiting.

Soon enough, her breathing deepens into sleep.

Returning Inward

You sink back into the gem.

Your layered structure greets you like familiar terrain now.

The outer pool drifts slowly with ambient magic from the forest.

The first ring holds its firm curve, the endurance of the trader’s road shaping the flow.

The second ring guides currents with calm stability, the memory of tunnels and steady work smoothing every movement.

The third lattice glints beneath it all—sharp intersections born from the moment before the blade fell.

And deeper still…

The core rests.

Your earliest memories sit there like bedrock beneath everything else.

Warmth.

Breath.

The safety of your mother’s scales.

The laughter of hatchlings in dirt tunnels.

You spend hours reinforcing that foundation—not enlarging it, but ensuring the currents slide over it naturally, as if the gem itself had grown around that point.

The Reservoir Deepens

You make careful adjustments.

Not bold changes.

Tiny refinements.

You smooth where pressure gathers too quickly.

You sharpen intersections in the lattice so that violent currents would break apart before reaching the core.

You even shape small spiral eddies in the outer pool so that when the gem refills from the forest’s magic, the flow distributes evenly.

Gradually the entire system behaves like a well-built reservoir.

Energy gathers.

Circulates.

Feeds the staff when called.

But the deepest water remains untouched.

The Bones

As you work, your thoughts return to the bones you saw hanging at the hill.

The skull.

The rib.

The femur.

The pelvis buried in dirt.

You consider what became of the rest.

Some likely scattered by animals.

Some perhaps burned in the witch’s rituals.

Some ground into powder in the jars lining her shelves.

You remember seeing a mortar stained dark with old bone dust.

Perhaps pieces of you have already passed through her potions… dissolved into spells long forgotten.

The thought is strange.

Your body once moved through the tunnels of your warren.

Now parts of it might be scattered through the forest soil… or drifting in the veins of people who drank her brews.

Yet some pieces remain.

And those pieces remember.

Not your mind.

But the shape of what you were.

If the gem ever shattered…

Perhaps those echoes could matter.

Not as strongly as the skull.

But together…

Maybe enough.

The Quiet Hours

You spend the rest of the night refining the reservoir.

Testing how currents behave when imagined surges push through them.

Ensuring that if the staff ever tried to consume everything inside the gem, the outer layers would collapse first—feeding the surge—while the core sealed itself completely.

The system holds.

Not perfect.

But strong.

Stronger than anything the witch suspects.

Dawn

Grey light creeps into the hut again.

The witch stirs, yawning and scratching her tangled hair.

She glances at the gem.

Just a quick look this morning.

“Reliable little stone,” she mutters.

She lifts the staff and steps outside.

Another day begins.

But something is different today.

Her pack is heavier.

More supplies.

More pouches.

And she glances north more than once while walking.

Toward the mountains.

Toward the place travelers spoke of.

The tower.

As the day begins, what do you focus on?
Observe travelers again, hoping to hear more news about the tower before the witch reaches it.
Watch the witch’s preparations closely, learning what spells or tools she plans to use there.
Listen carefully at the bone hill again, seeing if the forest watchers react to the tower’s awakening.
Study how the gem refills during travel, measuring the efficiency of your reservoir.
Continue mapping the land, preparing for the possibility of a long journey north.

The witch returns to the Hill of Bones before noon.

She plants the staff into the dirt.

The gem sways beneath it.

The bone-magic channel opens again, cold and heavy.

You reach outward immediately.

Not to the forest this time.

To the bones.

Listening Through the Body

Strength.

Balance.

The sense of weight shifting.

Heavy.

Grounded.

The bones answer.

Not in words.

What the Forest Knows

The first impression comes like cold wind through leaves.

Stone.

A tall shape rising above trees.

Broken.

Old.

The tower.

Light in the upper windows.

Not torchlight.

Something colder.

A pale glow that leaks from cracks in the stone.

The watchers do not like it.

The feeling carries something close to irritation.

Movement.

Not deer.

Something walking the stone paths around the tower.

Two-legged.

Stiff.

Unsteady.

Dead things walking.

Something beneath the tower.

Deep.

Buried.

Not new.

Not awake yet.

Roots and worms and burrowing creatures avoid the ground there.

Then nods.

She scatters another pinch of powder.

Something Notices You

Through rib.

Through femur.

Through the buried pelvis touching the roots.

The forest awareness brushes against you again.

Not hostile.

Not curious exactly.

A body.

The watchers cannot understand it.

Then the witch pulls the staff from the ground.

The magic breaks.

The forest presence withdraws.

What You Learned

As she walks away from the hill, your thoughts settle around the fragments of knowledge the forest shared:

• The tower is active again.
• Pale light burns in its upper levels.
• Walking dead move around it.
• Something older sleeps beneath the tower.

And the witch is clearly interested.

Her grip on the staff is tighter as she leaves the clearing.

Her mind already turning toward that distant ruin.

The bones sway gently behind you.

Your rib taps softly against its cord.

For a brief moment…

You feel the forest watchers still remembering the strange echo of a body that no longer lives.

The witch does not return to the hut immediately after leaving the Hill of Bones.

Instead, she walks a longer path through the forest—one you have rarely taken before. The ground slopes gradually upward, and the trees thin slightly, letting more grey daylight reach the moss below.

You sway beneath the staff as she walks.

And you watch.

The Witch Prepares

She stops first near a patch of black-rooted herbs growing between stones.

She kneels slowly and begins harvesting them.

Not roughly.

Carefully.

Each root pulled intact.

Each wrapped in cloth before being placed in her satchel.

You feel a faint pulse of earth magic when she touches them.

Protective herbs.

Not offensive.

Later she gathers something else.

A cluster of pale mushrooms growing from a fallen log.

These you recognize.

You saw them once in a jar in the hut.

She uses them in potions meant to resist corruption.

Again…

Not offensive magic.

Defensive.

As the day continues she collects several other ingredients:

• Iron filings from a small pouch she checks carefully.
• A small bottle of oil you recognize from earlier spells of warding.
• A strip of cloth wrapped around something heavy—likely silver or bone.

Each item goes into her pack with deliberate care.

She is not wandering.

She is preparing.

She practices only one spell today.

A short ward whispered over the staff itself.

You feel the energy draw through the reservoir you built.

The outer layers feed the magic easily.

The lattice compresses the deeper pressure.

The core remains untouched.

She nods to herself.

“Good.”

Satisfied.

Your Question

As she works, you find yourself turning over the thought that has been bothering you.

Why?

Why would someone like this care about a necromancer’s tower?

This is the same woman who killed you without hesitation.

Who traps souls.

Who bargains with the forest through bone and blood.

A witch.

Not a hero.

The answer comes slowly as you observe her habits more carefully.

She does not act like someone preparing to fight a necromancer.

She acts like someone preparing to visit one.

Or at least to approach something dangerous carefully.

You begin to notice patterns in her muttering as she gathers ingredients.

She speaks mostly to herself.

But sometimes…

You catch fragments.

“…if he has awakened something…”

“…dangerous to leave unchecked…”

The last phrase catches your attention.

Not wrong.

Not evil.

Just dangerous.

A Different Kind of Self-Interest

You begin to understand.

The witch is not concerned because she is good.

She is concerned because she is practical.

The forest is her domain.

Her power.

Her safety.

A necromancer raising the dead in a nearby ruin threatens that balance.

Walking corpses disrupt the forest.

Disturb spirits.

Drive away animals.

Even anger the watchers she bargains with.

And if something deeper sleeps beneath the tower…

That could threaten everything nearby.

Including her.

She mutters again while packing the last of her herbs.

“Better to see what fool has woken it…”

She taps the staff against a rock.

“…before it grows teeth.”

The Road Ahead

By the time evening approaches, her pack is much heavier.

She looks north again.

Toward the mountains you know lie beyond the forest.

Toward the tower the forest watchers spoke of.

She is not leaving tonight.

But soon.

Very soon.

Inside the gem, your reservoir remains stable.

Your sabotage plan sits quietly in your thoughts.

If she attempts powerful magic at the tower…

The moment you have prepared for may finally come.

The hut comes back into view as the sun lowers.

She enters.

The staff returns to its hook.

The night approaches again.

The hut grows quiet again.

The witch sleeps heavily tonight, one arm draped across her chest, breath rasping softly through her nose. The fire has gone nearly dark, leaving the room lit only by faint red coals.

The gem rests.

Preparing the Collapse

You do not strengthen the reservoir outward.

That would draw attention.

Instead, you refine how it fails.

You study the pathways again—outer pool, rings, lattice, core—and imagine the moment when the staff tries to consume everything.

A catastrophic surge.

The conduit rune opening fully.

The regulators failing.

The dampeners overheating.

The staff drawing harder and harder until the gem empties.

You reshape the flow so that, when that moment comes…

the outer layers give way intentionally.

Not violently.

Not like a wall breaking.

More like a dam opening its floodgates.

Energy would pour outward in a sudden rush—feeding the staff faster than it expects.

To any observer, it would look like the gem had simply reached its limit.

Drained.

Spent.

Dead.

The Hidden Seal

While the outer layers collapse, the lattice performs its second task.

It compresses inward.

Each sharp intersection locks against the next, forming a sealed cage around the deepest layer.

The core.

The earliest memory.

The place the control rune cannot reach.

You refine this closure slowly, testing each imagined pressure point.

The collapse must appear natural.

The gem must look burned out.

Not sabotaged.

What Remains

When the collapse completes in your simulations, the result is simple.

To the witch:

A dead gem.

A drained soul battery.

Nothing left to draw from.

Inside, however…

a tiny spark remains.

Your hidden core.

Almost completely cut off from the outer currents.

The gem would refill eventually, but with the circulation pathways sealed, the process would be painfully slow.

Not weeks.

Perhaps longer.

You cannot know.

The core would survive.

The skull holds memory.

The femur holds strength.

Movement.

Balance.

Form.

Not like having a living body again.

A quiet possibility forms in your mind.

If the gem ever dies…

And the core survives…

Perhaps the bones could serve as points of return.

Fragments of a body waiting for something to bind them together again.

You do not yet know how such a thing could be done.

The outer layers behave exactly as they always have.

Strong.

Reliable.

Toward the tower.

The witch leaves the forest behind by mid-morning.

For the first time since your death, the world opens wider than a few familiar trails.

The road north is rough but clear—two deep wagon ruts carved through packed earth, with grass growing in the middle where wheels rarely pass. Hills roll gently outward, and the thick forest slowly gives way to scattered stands of trees and wide stretches of wind-bent grass.

You sway beneath the staff as she walks.

And you watch.

The Wider World

The land feels larger out here.

You see things you only knew as distant stories when you were alive.

Stone fences marking old farm boundaries.

A ruined watchtower crumbling into weeds beside the road.

Smoke rising from a distant hamlet far off across the hills.

Once, you pass a small shrine beside the road—a carved stone figure weathered almost smooth by time. Travelers have left coins and dried flowers at its base.

The witch barely glances at it.

She walks like someone used to moving through the world alone.

People on the Road

The road carries more travelers than the forest ever did.

A merchant wagon passes in the afternoon.

Two drivers on the bench, a guard walking beside the rear axle with a spear across his shoulder.

They eye the witch carefully.

Not friendly.

Not hostile either.

Just cautious.

One of them mutters under his breath as they pass:

“Don’t make deals with hedge witches.”

The other replies quietly:

“Don’t make enemies either.”

The wagon rolls on.

Later a pair of pilgrims walks south.

Simple robes.

Walking sticks.

They bow politely as they pass her.

The witch nods once in return.

She does not stop for conversation.

Watching the Witch

You observe her closely during the journey.

She walks steadily, rarely pausing.

Her senses are sharper.

She watches ridgelines.

Listens to the wind.

The road north is not her home.

And she knows it.

The bone sitting on that shelf in the hut.

If the staff breaks.

The witch lived there alone.

A silent witness.

A waiting anchor.

Toward the bones you left behind.

The rib.

The femur.

Hills grow steeper.

Far in the distance.

Jagged walls.

A tower.

A cold, pale light.

The witch stops walking.

Her eyes narrow slightly.

The witch does not rush toward the tower.

When the ruined spire first appears on the ridge ahead, she slows her pace instead.

The road winds upward through broken hills now. Stone juts from the earth like old bones, and the grass grows thin between patches of grey soil. The wind carries a different smell here—dry dust, old stone, and something faintly sour beneath it.

You watch her carefully.

The Witch Prepares

She stops at the edge of a shallow ravine about half a mile from the tower.

Close enough to see it clearly.

Far enough that nothing from the ruins could easily reach her.

She sets her pack down and kneels.

For several minutes she says nothing.

She simply watches the tower.
