First she takes out the iron filings you saw earlier.

A small circle is scratched into the dirt with the tip of her knife.

The filings are sprinkled into the circle carefully.

Iron wards.

Protection against certain kinds of spirits.

Next comes the pale mushrooms.

She crushes them between two stones and mixes the paste with a dark liquid from a vial.

You feel the faint ripple of defensive magic when she drinks it.

A potion against corruption.

Perhaps against necromantic influence.

Then she unwraps the cloth bundle.

Inside lies a small object.

A silver charm shaped like a stylized skull.

It is bound to the staff just beneath the gem with a thin wire.

You feel a new rune flare briefly as she does this.

A reinforcement.

Something meant to strengthen soul magic defenses.

Ironically, it strengthens the stability of the gem.

Of you.

Finally she plants the staff in the dirt and whispers a longer spell.

The draw from the gem begins.

You watch the currents carefully.

Outer pool → first ring → second ring → lattice.

The pressure increases more than any spell she has cast before.

But the reservoir holds perfectly.

The magic flows upward.

A translucent shimmer spreads across her skin like faint frost.

A protective ward.

She exhales slowly.

“That should do.”

Studying the Tower

Now that she has finished preparing, you turn your attention outward.

The tower stands on a rocky hill surrounded by crumbling stone walls—once part of a fortress, long abandoned.

The structure is tall but broken.

The upper levels lean slightly.

Several windows glow with the pale light the travelers described.

Not firelight.

Too steady.

Too cold.

You focus your awareness outward as far as it will stretch.

Your range is still limited to the space around the gem.

But from the witch’s vantage point you can see much.

The road continues upward through a broken gate.

Beyond the gate…

Movement.

The Dead

Three shapes wander the courtyard below the tower.

Humanoid.

Clumsy.

Their movements are stiff and wrong.

Rotting cloth hangs from their bodies.

One drags a rusted spear.

Another turns slowly in place as if listening for something it cannot quite hear.

The third simply stands facing the tower wall.

The watchers in the forest had spoken true.

These are walking dead.

But they are not the most interesting thing you notice.

Near the base of the tower door lies something else.

A shape that does not move at all.

Too large for a person.

Too misshapen for a corpse.

Something like bones and armor piled together in a twisted mass.

Waiting.

The Witch Watches

The witch studies the ruins carefully.

She crouches low, resting one elbow on her knee.

Her eyes move slowly across the courtyard.

Then she mutters quietly.

“Hmph.”

Her tone is thoughtful rather than frightened.

“Sloppy work.”

She stands again.

Grips the staff.

And begins walking toward the broken gate.

The dead figures in the courtyard have not yet noticed her.

But they will soon.

Inside the gem, your reservoir remains calm.

Your collapse plan waits silently beneath the currents.

If she draws too deeply…

If the staff surges…

Everything you built may soon be tested.

As the witch approaches the ruined gate, what do you focus on?
Watch the undead closely, studying how they move and react.
Study the strange bone pile near the tower door, trying to understand what it is.
Monitor the witch’s magic flow carefully, anticipating the moment she casts.
Listen to the ambient magic around the tower, sensing what lies beneath it.
Watch the witch’s body language, learning how cautious she truly is.

The witch advances slowly toward the broken gate.

Not to the walking dead.

The Magic of the Land

You have learned what magic feels like in different places.

The forest near the hut was thick with life magic—soft, drifting threads tied to roots, animals, flowing water, and the old watchers beneath the soil.

The road through the hills carried far less magic. Thin strands moved through the air like dust in sunlight, replenishing the gem slowly but steadily.

But here…

The magic is different.

Very different.

The Tower’s Aura

As you stretch your senses outward, the air around the ruins feels like a pond whose surface has been disturbed by many stones.

Currents twist against each other.

Cold flows slide over warmer ones.

Others sink into the earth beneath the hill.

Old.

Heavy.

The forest watchers were right.

Something lies beneath this place.

Something that has been there longer than the tower itself.

Something that does not like being disturbed.

Necromantic Magic

You also feel another layer woven through the chaos.

Necromantic magic.

Not elegant.

Not carefully structured like the witch’s spells.

This magic is forced.

Threads of power pulled violently from the dead bodies scattered through the ruins.

The magic feels brittle.

Like ropes stretched too tight.

You suspect whoever is controlling it is powerful enough to animate corpses…

…but not skilled enough to do it cleanly.

The Witch’s First Spell

The moment the first undead notices her, the witch stops walking.

The corpse with the rusted spear jerks its head toward her.

Then begins stumbling forward.

The other two follow.

The witch raises the staff.

The conduit rune opens.

You feel the draw begin.

Spell One — Bone Severance

This is a stronger spell than anything she has used on the road.

Energy pulls quickly through the reservoir.

Outer pool → first ring → second ring.

The gem flares green.

The spear-carrying corpse collapses instantly.

Not burned.

Not shattered.

Its bones simply fall apart, dropping into a loose pile.

The magic has severed the necromantic binding holding it together.

Efficient.

Observing the Draw

You watch the currents carefully.

This spell drained far more power than the road charms.

But your reservoir behaves exactly as planned.

The outer layers feed the spell.

The deeper layers compress the flow.

The core remains untouched.

Refilling

As the spell ends, the gem begins drawing ambient magic again.

Here…

The refill behaves differently.

The chaotic magic around the tower actually feeds the gem faster than the forest did.

But it is unstable.

Wild currents flow into the outer pool unevenly.

Your rings redirect them smoothly, preventing turbulence from reaching deeper layers.

Without your work…

This environment might have damaged the gem over time.

The Fight Continues

The second corpse rushes her.

She does not move.

A small fire spell erupts.

Another strong draw from the gem.

The corpse ignites and collapses into burning cloth and blackened bone.

Closer now.

The strange bone-and-armor pile near the tower door remains still.

Tense.

Waiting.

But the air around the tower grows thicker with unstable magic.

Growth.

The Deep Magic

The residue of long-forgotten rituals.

Heavy.

Old beyond anything you have sensed before.

Whoever built the fortress long ago likely knew something was here.

Not waking.

The forest watchers were aware.

Does neither.

It is not watching.

Not listening.

A reservoir of ancient power buried beneath stone.

The Grounding Rune

The core will seal.

You will survive.

The staff’s enchantments were never designed for this.

Even the witch might hesitate to draw from it directly.

What the Book Contains

The magic patterns reveal fragments of the book’s contents.

Not word-for-word.

Technique.

Purpose.

Corpse Anchors

The simplest spells are the ones you already observed.

Small necromantic knots inserted into corpses.

Each knot acts like a hook for the caster’s will.

That explains the crude undead wandering the courtyard.

The book likely contains diagrams showing how to place those anchors in bone or muscle.

The method is inefficient—but easy to learn.

Energy Siphons

Another section of the book describes ritual circles designed to draw power from places saturated with death.

Graveyards.

Battlefields.

Ancient ruins.

The tower ritual you saw was a larger version of this.

The necromancer simply chose a far more dangerous source than they understood.

Control Threads

A more interesting technique appears deeper in the book.

Instead of controlling each corpse individually…

The necromancer experimented with binding several undead to a central thread of magic.

Like puppets connected to the same string.

That method would allow a caster to control dozens of undead with far less effort.

All the undead collapse at once.

One pattern in the book catches your attention.

It is not about raising corpses.

Not the same ritual the witch used on you.

Temporary.

Used to store fragments of consciousness inside bones or talismans.

A crude attempt at soul anchoring.

But the concept is similar.

The necromancer’s methods show that souls can attach to multiple anchors if the magic is structured correctly.

Not easily.

But possible.

Your skull.

Your rib.

Your femur.

Your buried pelvis.

The pieces of your body still scattered in the forest.

The idea of a distributed anchor becomes slightly less impossible.

Despite these discoveries, the necromancer’s work is incomplete.

Much of the magic in the book is theoretical.

Copied from older texts.

The caster clearly lacked the experience to execute many of the rituals safely.

Which explains the unstable circle upstairs.

And why the witch called his work “sloppy.”

Inside the pouch, the gem lies among chalk dust and cracked glass.

But deep inside the sealed core, you shift your attention inward again.

Holding the Stone “Dead”

Normally, even a spent focus stone would begin to refill slowly.

Ambient magic always leaks into enchanted objects. Especially at night, when currents move more freely through the land.

You can already feel it.

Thin threads of energy brushing against the gem’s outer shell as the witch walks through town.

If those currents began circulating again, the stone might faintly glow.

Someone might notice.

So you reshape the collapsed layers slightly.

Not opening them.

Instead, you build tiny pressure walls along the outer pool—small inward folds that redirect any incoming magic back outward again.

Ambient currents touch the gem…

Then slide away.

Like rain running off polished glass.

Nothing accumulates.

Nothing circulates.

To anyone examining the stone, it will remain completely inert.

Dead.

Nothing powerful.

Nothing threatening.

Just everyday magic meant to keep a small settlement safe.

Your prison.

Your disguise.

Refining the Dead Stone

The outer shell of the gem already rejects incoming magic.

But you realize something important:

A true dead focus stone would not only fail to absorb magic… it would also fail to hold any.

So you begin shaping something more sophisticated than simple rejection.

You construct a two-layer silence.

The First Barrier — Reflection

The outermost layer behaves like polished glass.

When ambient magic touches the gem, it does not enter.

Instead it slides across the surface and continues outward into the surrounding currents.

To magical senses, the gem will feel inert.

Empty.

As if its internal channels collapsed permanently when the staff exploded.

The Second Barrier — Containment

Beneath that reflective shell, you form a second structure.

A quiet pocket surrounding the sealed reservoir.

This one does the opposite.

If any magic somehow slips inward…

It cannot escape.

It would become trapped in small circulating loops inside the collapsed outer pool.

Never reaching the deeper rings.

Never touching the core.

Never leaking outward.

From the outside, the stone would remain perfectly inert.

Even if something were inside.

The Result

The structure becomes something unusual.

A magical void shell.

Magic does not enter.

Magic does not leave.

It simply passes around the gem like water flowing around a smooth stone in a river.

Only if you deliberately release the barriers would the gem behave like a focus again.

A Useful Side Effect

You notice something interesting as you test the structure.

Because the outer layers are now sealed so tightly, the control rune’s influence weakens further.

The rune was designed to dominate the gem’s internal flow.

But now there is no flow to dominate.

Your core rests deeper than ever.

Silent.

Hidden.

Untouchable.

No magic out.

Knot

Echo stabilization.

Your skull.

Inside the pouch, you turn inward immediately.

Divine magic is different from anything you have encountered before. The witch’s magic was structured and disciplined. The necromancer’s was crude and violent. Even the ancient reservoir beneath the tower felt like raw, sleeping power.

Divine magic… is something else entirely.

So before the priest even enters the room, you examine your disguise again.

Reinforcing the Dead Stone

You review each layer carefully.

Outer Reflection Shell
Ambient magic touches the gem and slides away. No absorption. No resonance. Any magical sense should feel only inert mineral—like polished onyx or obsidian.

Containment Pocket
If even a trace of magic slips through the outer layer, it cannot escape again. It circulates harmlessly in shallow loops without touching the deeper rings.

Collapsed Reservoir
The outer structures remain shattered and dormant, exactly like a soul gem that burned out during catastrophic overload.

Hidden Core
Buried far beneath everything else, wrapped in your earliest memories. No current reaches it. No rune touches it. No magic leaks from it.

You make one final addition.

A faint echo scar.

A subtle pattern in the collapsed layers that mimics what happens when a bound soul is destroyed during magical backlash.

To anyone examining the gem, it will appear that:

• The gem once held a soul
• The soul burned away during the explosion
• The gem’s structure collapsed afterward

Exactly what the witch believes happened.

The Nature of Divine Magic

The first thing you notice is how stable it is.

Arcane magic flows.

It bends, twists, circulates through runes and channels.

Necromantic magic claws and hooks into things.

It radiates.

Like warmth from a hearth.

The priest himself is not forcing the power outward. Instead the magic seems to exist around him naturally, anchored through his faith and whatever force answers it.

It spreads through the room in gentle layers.

And then fades.

The warmth you noticed earlier returns faintly.

Safety.

Clarity.

It tries to pull attention toward it.

Not aggressively.

But persistently.

It simply aligns the mind toward calm and focus.

For someone steeped in divine magic, this probably helps them sense corruption, undeath, or spiritual disturbance.

But because you are sealed inside the gem, the effect barely reaches you.

You can examine it without being pulled in.

How It Senses

You watch how the magic behaved when the priest held the gem.

The divine magic did not probe like a spellcaster searching with runes.

Instead it compared spiritual patterns.

Living soul.

Undead corruption.

Bound spirit.

Divine energy.

Your void shell presented a different pattern entirely:

• collapsed magical lattice
• burned-out soul scar
• inert mineral core

To the divine sense, the gem appeared empty.

Not corrupted.

Not haunted.

Simply ruined.

That is why the priest returned it without concern.

A Critical Insight

Divine magic seems especially sensitive to undeath and trapped souls.

But it looks for those through resonance.

Presence.

Spiritual echo.

Your design hides both.

Your soul sits behind several layers of:

• collapsed channels
• reflective shell
• containment loops
• memory core

To the priest’s magic, it is as though the soul that once powered the gem simply burned away completely.

Which happens often enough in magical catastrophes that it raises no alarm.

Unlike arcane magic, the divine energy does not swirl or search.

Just acknowledgment.

Alive.

Satisfied.

You now understand something important.

Divine magic detects three main things:

• Undeath – corruption, decay, necromantic binding
• Active souls – living or trapped
• Sacred resonance – divine presence or blessing

Your disguise successfully mimics a fourth category:

• Spent soul vessel

Something that once held a soul… but no longer does.

As long as your core remains hidden beneath the collapsed lattice, divine magic will accept that explanation.

Morning creeps slowly into the captain’s hall.

Boots shuffle. A guard yawns loudly near the door. Someone pokes at the embers in the hearth, sending sparks drifting up the chimney. The town outside wakes in stages—wagon wheels, chickens, the distant hammer of a smith beginning the day.

Inside the pouch, the gem remains exactly what everyone believes it to be.

A dead stone.

But your awareness stretches outward again.

Not toward the skull.

Toward the book.

Studying the Book in Daylight

The necromancer’s book still lies on the captain’s table where Father Halric left it the night before.

The captain himself sits nearby now, rubbing sleep from his eyes and drinking bitter morning tea while he flips through the pages.

Every turn of the paper sends vibrations through the table.

Through the floor.

Through the pouch.

Enough for you to continue studying the contents.

The Anchor Chapters

The captain lingers over several diagrams you have already partially reconstructed.

Now, with repeated exposure, you refine them.

The theory behind multi-anchor souls becomes clearer.

The book describes two types of anchors:

Primary Anchor

The vessel containing the true knot of the soul.

If destroyed, the soul risks collapse.

Resonant Anchors

Objects that share strong identity patterns with the soul.

These can hold fragments of awareness or act as pathways for movement.

But they must contain true memory imprint, not just magical preparation.

Your bones qualify perfectly.

They lived with you.

They remember you.

The Stability Rules

A few notes in the margins catch your attention.

Apparently many necromancers failed when attempting multi-anchor binding.

The book lists three common causes of failure:

• Distance strain — anchors too far apart weaken the thread
• Identity drift — anchors without matching memory patterns destabilize the soul
• Anchor imbalance — too much awareness in secondary anchors fractures the core

You immediately recognize the first problem.

Distance.

The skull anchor works, but the strain is real.

A Hidden Note

One passage near the bottom of a page appears written by the necromancer himself.

You feel the indentation of the ink where he pressed harder while writing.

“Bone anchors resonate naturally. Living vessels unnecessary if the skeleton is intact. Skull strongest. Pelvis stabilizes structure.”

That last line interests you.

You remember the pelvis half buried at the bone hill.

That bone may be far more important than you first thought.

Another Section

The captain turns to a different chapter.

This one concerns soul migration.

The necromancer was trying to learn how a bound spirit could move between anchors.

The diagrams show something like stepping stones across a river.

A soul can move between anchors if:

• the thread remains intact
• the anchors share resonance
• the soul transfers gradually, not all at once

Exactly what you began doing with the skull last night.

The Captain

The captain flips a few more pages and scowls.

“Gods below…”

He shuts the book briefly and mutters to himself.

“Priest better get here soon.”

He clearly understands enough to know the book is dangerous.

But not enough to grasp its deeper details.

Which works in your favor.

A New Sound

Outside the hall, hooves clatter against the dirt road.

Several riders have arrived.

The captain looks toward the door.

“About time.”

The door opens moments later.

Father Halric enters again.

Behind him…

another presence.

Heavier steps.

Armor.

A deeper voice.

“Captain.”

The captain stands immediately.

“Father. And…?”

“Bishop’s envoy,” the priest says.

The room grows quieter.

The book remains on the table.

Open.

Still being studied.

And now a new authority has arrived.

Watching the Shape of Divine Magic

Unlike arcane magic, which forms visible patterns through runes, gestures, and channels, the envoy’s divine magic originates inside him.

A spiritual center.

Not constant.

Not automatic.

It responds to focus.

The Three Layers

As you study him, you begin recognizing three distinct behaviors in his divine magic.

1. The Passive Field

This is the calm warmth you felt earlier.

It spreads naturally around him a few paces in every direction.

This layer does not search.

It simply exists.

Within it, divine magic quietly notices things that are wrong:

• undead
• cursed objects
• trapped souls
• demonic influence

But it only alerts the wielder. It does not act.

Father Halric relies mostly on this layer.

2. The Focused Thread

The envoy uses this layer when inspecting objects.

You watched it when he examined the gem.

A thin line of divine magic forms in his hand and flows outward like a probe.

This thread reads magical structures:

• bindings
• runic patterns
• necromantic knots
• spiritual anchors

It is surgical.

Precise enough to read the structure of magic without breaking it.

This is the layer that could become dangerous if it ever reached your inner lattice.

3. The Purging Strike

You haven’t seen him use it yet.

But you feel its presence.

A much heavier concentration of divine magic sits coiled deep inside him.

Not moving.

Not probing.

Just waiting.

If unleashed, it would likely manifest as:

• a radiant burst
• purification magic
• destruction of undead or corrupted magic

This is the magic of someone trained to fight necromancers directly.

How He Controls It

You watch the transitions.

The envoy does not use gestures or incantations.

Instead, he does three things:

Focus
His mind narrows when he inspects something.

Breath
His breathing slows and deepens.

Intent
The divine magic responds strongly to purpose.

Unlike arcane magic, which follows rules of structure and formula…

Divine magic responds to alignment between will and belief.

When he believes something must be examined, the thread forms.

When he believes something must be destroyed, the deeper power would likely awaken.

A Crucial Weakness

You notice something interesting.

The divine thread he used earlier never dug deeper than the first coherent structure it encountered.

When it encountered the scar of the burned-out gem, it stopped there.

It accepted the explanation the structure provided.

Divine magic does not question structure the way arcane analysis does.

It assumes the spiritual truth presented to it.

Your illusion works because it tells a believable story:

A soul once existed.

The soul is gone.

The vessel is broken.

i practice with the divine magic more, and study its reactions.. and see if i can refine the inner core to better deceive it if needed

Inside the pouch, the gem lies as lifeless as ever.

Boots move across the captain’s hall. Chairs scrape. The envoy and the priest continue discussing riders, maps, and the ruined tower. None of it touches the stone.

But within the sealed shell of your prison, you open the reflection layer once again—only a hair’s breadth—and allow another whisper of the envoy’s divine field to slip inside.

Then you seal it.

Warmth spreads through the containment loops.

You begin your work.

Learning the Nature of Divine Magic

You no longer simply observe the divine fragment. Now you experiment with it deliberately.

The first thing you test is shape.

You gather the warmth into a thread again, the way the envoy did when examining the gem. It takes effort—your focus must remain steady—but the divine current responds when your intent becomes clear.

Thread.

Release.

Thread again.

Each time it forms slightly faster.

Divine magic, you realize, does not like confusion. If your purpose is uncertain, it dissolves back into passive warmth. But if your will is firm—even if your technique is crude—it aligns with that purpose.

You begin to understand the envoy’s discipline.

It is not complicated magic.

It is certain magic.

Testing the Illusion

Once you can form the thread reliably, you begin testing your disguise more aggressively.

You guide the divine thread toward the illusion scar—the pattern you constructed to resemble a soul burned away in magical backlash.

The divine magic brushes the scar.

The reaction is the same each time:

• calm acceptance
• recognition of a departed soul
• no further probing

The illusion is working.

But you want it stronger.

Refining the False Scar

You reshape the outer lattice carefully.

Not changing the story it tells—only refining the details.

You add subtle irregularities to the collapsed channels.

Tiny fractures where the ritual backlash supposedly cracked the gem’s internal structure.

Residual echo patterns that resemble the fading memory of a soul that has already passed on.

The result becomes more convincing.

When the divine thread touches it again, the warmth settles deeper into the scar pattern.

Satisfied.

As though the divine magic itself agrees with the story.

A Dangerous Boundary

Curiosity pushes the thread slightly deeper.

Closer to the hidden lattice guarding your core.

The reaction is immediate.

The divine thread brightens sharply.

Not hostile—but alert.

It senses order beneath the ruin.

You withdraw it instantly.

The warmth softens again as it returns to the outer scar.

Lesson learned.

Your disguise works because the divine magic stops when it finds a believable explanation.

If it ever pushes deeper…

The hidden structures might be revealed.

A New Possibility

While shaping the divine thread, you discover something interesting.

Divine magic reacts not just to structure…

but to moral narrative.

When you guide the thread across the scar while holding the idea of:

A soul destroyed by reckless magic

The divine current settles comfortably.

When you guide it with the thought of:

A soul trapped and suffering

The thread grows tense and alert.

Divine magic responds to meaning as much as pattern.

Your illusion works not only because the structure looks right…

but because the story it tells feels morally resolved.

The soul is gone.

No suffering remains.

Outside the Pouch

The envoy finishes speaking with the captain.

“Riders leave at dawn.”

Father Halric nods.

“I’ll remain here with the prisoner.”

The envoy glances toward the pouch one last time before heading toward the door.

He shows no suspicion.

To him, the stone is nothing more than a dead magical tool.

Inside the Gem

Your divine fragment dissolves slowly back into passive warmth.

You release it through the shell, letting it return to the envoy’s ambient field before sealing the barrier again.

The gem becomes completely inert once more.

But now you know something vital.

If divine magic ever examines you again…

You can guide the story it reads.

What do you do next?
Continue practicing with divine magic, learning to shape stronger threads of it.
Strengthen the skull anchor again, improving your ability to act through it.
Study the necromancer’s book further, focusing on the multi-anchor skeleton theory.
Extend awareness toward the bone hill, testing the rib, femur, and pelvis anchors.
Observe the witch overnight, judging whether she might attempt escape before the riders leave.
i spend the rest of the night with the necromancy book.. no telling what they will do about it afterwards, so might be the last chance, as disturbing as some of the stuff is

The night stretches long inside the captain’s hall.

Lanterns burn low. One guard snores softly near the door. Another sits half-awake with his spear across his knees. Outside, the town settles into the slow breathing of sleeping buildings and distant wind through the palisade.

The pouch sits forgotten on a bench.

The gem inside remains a dead stone.

But your awareness reaches outward again.

Toward the book.

The Last Night with the Book

You realize something important very quickly.

The envoy will take this book in the morning.

Either to the bishop…

Or to a fire.

Texts like this rarely survive long once the church takes interest.

So you study it with the intensity of someone reading a map before it burns.

The True Purpose of the Book

The necromancer who wrote these notes was not merely animating corpses.

That was only the surface work.

Deeper in the book, scattered across several pages, you find the real obsession.

Persistence.

The necromancer feared death.

Every major section of the book ultimately connects back to the same goal:

How to keep the self alive beyond the body.

The Skeleton Network

One long passage confirms something you suspected earlier.

A skeleton provides a natural resonance structure.

Each bone contains traces of the life it once supported.

If arranged correctly, the skeleton can act as a distributed soul vessel.

The book suggests a theoretical structure:

• Skull – seat of identity
• Spine / pelvis – stabilizing anchor
• Ribs – resonance amplifiers
• Limbs – extension points for influence

The necromancer never completed the design.

But the theory is clear.

A soul could anchor itself across the bones of its former body.

Not trapped in one vessel…

But distributed.

Difficult to destroy.

Difficult even to find.

Soul Migration

Another section describes the process of moving awareness between anchors.

The necromancer compares it to crossing a river on stepping stones.

The soul never leaps directly.

Instead it moves gradually:

Core → anchor → anchor → anchor

Each movement leaves behind a smaller echo.

Exactly like what you began doing with the skull.

The Danger

Several warnings appear in the margins.

These are written more hastily, as if the necromancer learned them through painful mistakes.

You feel the pressure of the pen through the page as the captain turns it.

“Too much awareness outside core weakens primary knot.”

“Anchors must share true memory resonance or soul fractures.”

“Do not attempt migration during magical instability.”

You understand why.

A fractured soul might scatter permanently.

The Final Section

Near the end of the book, the necromancer speculates about something even more ambitious.

If a soul can anchor across bones…

Why not other objects?

Jewelry.

Weapons.

Amulets.

Even places of power.

But he admits the difficulty.

Without true memory imprint, such anchors become unstable.

That is why bones work best.

They lived with you.

They remember you.

A Grim Realization

One passage near the end is written in darker ink.

Possibly added later.

“Soul stones are inefficient prisons.
Skeleton anchor networks far superior.
If core survives, body destruction irrelevant.”

You sit with that thought for a long time.

Because that is exactly what you are beginning to build.

Dawn Approaches

The captain finally closes the book near dawn.

He rubs his eyes and mutters:

“Gods… what kind of madness is this.”

He leaves the book on the table.

But riders are already preparing outside.

You hear horses.

Harnesses.

Men speaking quietly.

The envoy will soon return.

And the book will likely leave with him.

Inside the pouch, the gem remains inert.

But during the night you have absorbed nearly everything the necromancer managed to write.

Not perfectly.

But enough.

Enough to continue the work yourself.

What do you do as dawn arrives?
Strengthen the skull anchor further, preparing to shift awareness there for longer periods.
Begin reaching toward the other bones (rib, femur, pelvis) to form a wider anchor network.
Observe the envoy and riders leaving for the tower, listening for what they plan to do.
Watch the witch, sensing whether she plans to escape before the investigation returns.
Experiment internally with divine magic again, refining your ability to control it.
i observe the envoy and riders the envoy says to bring the witches things. to see if any of it might have been used in the ritual. he notices the place for the stone on the staff is interchangeable.. like she uses a lot of them


Dawn creeps gray and cold through the shutters of the captain’s hall.

The guards change shifts. The smell of porridge and stale ale drifts faintly from somewhere nearby. Outside, horses stamp and snort as the riders prepare.

Inside the pouch, the gem remains dark and inert.

You listen.

The Riders Assemble

Boots and armor clink as the envoy returns.

The captain stands as he enters.

“Men are ready.”

The envoy nods once.

“Good.”

Father Halric stands beside the table, the necromancer’s book already wrapped in cloth.

“You’ll want this,” the priest says.

“Yes.”

The envoy takes the wrapped book and tucks it under his arm.

Then he pauses.

“And the witch’s belongings.”

The captain glances toward the bench.

“You mean the pouch?”

“And the staff.”

The Staff

A guard brings the broken staff pieces from the evidence rack where they were placed overnight.

The wood is cracked where the magical channels ruptured.

But the head of the staff remains mostly intact.

The envoy takes it carefully.

He turns it over in his hands.

Examining it.

The Interchangeable Mount

His brow furrows.

“Interesting.”

The captain steps closer.

“What?”

The envoy twists the metal ring at the head of the staff.

With a soft click…

The housing where the gem once sat rotates slightly.

Then slides free.

Not broken.

Designed.

A removable socket.

The envoy studies it closely.

“This isn’t a single focus housing.”

The captain frowns.

“What do you mean?”

The envoy holds the mount up in the lantern light.

“The socket is interchangeable.”

He turns it again.

Small grooves line the inside of the ring.

Wear marks.

Many.

“This staff was built to accept multiple stones.”

The captain’s eyes widen slightly.

“She carries more than one?”

The envoy shrugs faintly.

“Or did.”

The Implication

Father Halric frowns.

“That suggests preparation.”

“Yes,” the envoy replies.

“Repeated use.”

The captain looks toward the holding room door.

“She said the stone belonged to the necromancer.”

The envoy doesn’t answer immediately.

He studies the staff another moment.

Then says quietly:

“This design suggests the opposite.”

A Dangerous Thought

He sets the staff down.

“If she built this herself…”

“…then she has used soul stones before.”

The room grows quiet again.

The Pouch

The envoy finally opens the pouch.

Objects shift.

Chalk.

Herbs.

Glass vials.

And the dead black gem.

He lifts it briefly again.

Examines it one more time.

Then drops it back into the pouch.

Still uninterested.

Still convinced it is nothing more than a burned-out stone.

The Orders

The envoy ties the pouch closed again.

“Bring all of it.”

He hands it to one of the riders.

“We’ll examine everything at the tower.”

The captain nods.

“And the witch?”

“She stays here.”

The envoy glances toward the door.

“If the tower confirms her story…”

“…we release her.”

“And if it doesn’t?”

The envoy mounts his cloak.

“Then we come back with questions.”

Departure

Moments later the riders leave.

Horses clatter through the gate.

Hooves fade down the northern road.

The pouch containing the gem now hangs from the saddle of one of the envoy’s men.

You are leaving the town.

Heading back toward the tower.

Inside the gem, your hidden core remains perfectly still.

But the journey north has begun again.

Toward the place where:

• the necromancer died
• the deep magic sleeps
• and the bones of your body still lie scattered

What do you do during the ride toward the tower?
Strengthen the skull anchor further, preparing to shift awareness there again.
Reach toward the rib, femur, and pelvis, attempting to form additional anchors.
Observe the riders and envoy closely, learning more about their abilities.
Practice shaping divine magic again, refining your control over it.
Study the memory of the necromancer’s book, reconstructing its diagrams in detail.
i observe the riders as we travel, seeing if any of them show any awareness of my presence, in the way the witch would. mostly concerned about the envoy

The road north stretches pale and damp beneath the morning sky.

Hooves strike a steady rhythm against packed dirt. Harness leather creaks. The smell of horse sweat and wet grass fills the air as the riders move away from the town.

The pouch hangs from a saddle behind the envoy’s horse.

Inside it, the gem rests among chalk dust and cracked glass vials.

Dead.

Silent.

Watching.

The Riders

You extend your awareness carefully through the pouch.

Not pushing too far. Just enough to feel the presences around you.

There are five riders in total.

The Envoy

Riding at the front.

His presence is the easiest to feel.

The disciplined coil of divine magic remains wrapped around him like a quiet blade waiting in its sheath.

It does not sweep the road.

It does not search the riders.

It simply exists, alert and controlled.

If anything unnatural entered its radius with malicious intent, it would likely react instantly.

But your disguise tells a different story.

A dead magical object.

And so the divine field ignores you.

The Guards

The other four riders are ordinary soldiers.

You test them one by one.

Their minds are quiet, focused on the road and their duties.

No magical awareness.

No arcane senses.

They cannot feel the gem any more than they could feel a pebble in their saddlebag.

The Envoy Again

You pay particular attention to him.

Watching for the same kind of sensitivity the witch once showed.

The witch had an instinct for magic.

She could feel disturbances.

Feel power being drawn.

Feel rituals forming.

The envoy…

Is different.

His awareness is deliberate.

He does not constantly sense everything around him.

Instead, he inspects things when he chooses to.

When he does, the divine thread forms and examines the target.

Right now he is focused on the road.

On the tower ahead.

On the mission.

Your presence does not interest him.

Because you are presenting yourself as nothing.

Testing the Field

You gently brush the edges of his divine field.

Not pushing.

Just touching the warmth that extends outward from him.

The reaction is immediate—but subtle.

The divine warmth notices the gem.

It reads the illusion scar again.

Burned soul vessel.

Dead magic.

Nothing living.

The warmth drifts away.

Satisfied.

His Awareness

More interesting is what doesn’t happen.

The envoy never turns.

Never looks back at the pouch.

Never questions the stone again.

Once divine magic accepts a spiritual explanation…

It rarely questions it unless new evidence appears.

Your disguise has become part of the truth his senses believe.

The Road

The riders continue north for hours.

Fields give way to rough hills.

The land becomes quieter.

Less traveled.

Eventually the forest line appears in the distance.

The same forest that once held the witch’s hut.

The same forest where your bones still lie scattered.

The same forest where the tower waits.

A Familiar Pull

As the riders draw closer to the region, something else becomes noticeable.

The thread connecting you to the skull anchor grows stronger.

Distance strain fades.

The resonance deepens.

If you attempted a shift now…

It would likely hold much longer.

The envoy raises a hand.

The riders slow as the broken tower begins to rise above the trees ahead.

What do you do as you approach the tower again?
Shift awareness to the skull, taking advantage of the stronger connection.
Reach toward the other bones (rib, femur, pelvis) to begin forming a full anchor network.
Observe the envoy closely, studying how he prepares to enter the tower.
Practice shaping divine magic again, using the stronger divine field nearby.
Listen to the riders’ conversation, learning what they expect to find inside.
i reach towords the other bones now that they are closer and start making the network

The forest thickens as the riders leave the road.

Branches scrape lightly against armor. Hooves thud against soft earth. The ruined tower rises ahead through the trees like a broken tooth of stone.

And with every step the horses take…

The pull inside you grows stronger.

The thread to the skull hums now instead of whispering.

You are close.

Close enough that distance no longer strangles the connection.

So you reach farther.

Not just to the skull.

To the others.

Reaching the Rib

You follow the resonance outward from the skull anchor.

The bone hill lies not far from the hut—a tangled place of hanging bones and scattered remains where the witch once whispered to the dead.

Your awareness stretches along the skeleton’s forgotten map.

Then—

You feel it.

The rib.

Hanging from a cord.

Wind sways it gently.

The bone remembers the rhythm of breathing.

Your breathing.

You feed the resonance into it slowly.

Memory.

Identity.

A faint echo of life.

The rib responds quickly.

Not as strongly as the skull—but easily.

A third point appears in your structure.

A new anchor.

The Femur

Next you reach toward the dead tree where the femur rests.

This connection takes longer.

The bone lies partly buried in the hollow trunk.

Covered in moss.

But it still remembers weight.

Movement.

Walking.

Running.

The memory resonates.

You shape the echo carefully.

Another knot forms.

Not as strong as the skull.

Not as responsive as the rib.

But stable.

The Pelvis

The final piece is the hardest.

Half buried in dirt near the bone hill.

Covered in soil and time.

But the moment your awareness touches it, something interesting happens.

The resonance is stronger than expected.

The necromancer’s notes were correct.

The pelvis carries the structure of the body’s balance.

It remembers how everything connected.

The moment you feed the echo into it, the entire network tightens.

The Network Forms

Suddenly the structure becomes clearer.

Your anchors now form a crude skeleton network:

Primary Core:
Gem (true knot)

Secondary Anchors:
Skull – identity
Pelvis – structure

Resonance Anchors:
Rib – life rhythm
Femur – movement

Threads run between them.

The moment the pelvis stabilizes the network, the strain on the skull anchor drops dramatically.

Awareness flows more smoothly through the structure.

For a brief moment…

You exist in five places at once.

Gem.
Skull.
Pelvis.
Rib.
Femur.

Your mind does not fracture—but it stretches.

Expands.

The forest becomes easier to sense.

Wind through trees.

Insects moving through leaves.

The creak of the hut’s old wood.

The clack of the rib swaying gently on its cord.

A New Capability

You test something small.

Through the skull, you nudge the rib.

clack

The bone taps lightly against the branch.

Through the femur, you shift slightly in the hollow tree.

Leaves rustle.

Through the pelvis…

You feel the center of the network stabilizing everything.

The necromancer was right.

The skeleton remembers its shape.

Back at the Tower

Meanwhile the riders stop near the ruined tower.

The envoy dismounts.

“Spread out,” he orders.

“Check the grounds.”

The pouch sways as the soldier carrying it climbs down from his horse.

You hang from the saddle, unnoticed.

But now…

Your awareness stretches across the forest.

Across the hill.

Across your scattered bones.

You are no longer just a trapped soul in a gem.

You are becoming something distributed.

Something much harder to destroy.

What do you do now?
Strengthen the skeleton network, reinforcing the anchors while you are close to them.
Shift your awareness fully to the skull for a while, leaving only the core in the gem.
Observe the envoy and riders exploring the tower, they may disturb powerful magic.
Experiment with moving the bones, seeing how much influence you have through them.
Reach deeper into the magic beneath the tower, sensing the ancient reservoir again.

The riders spread out around the tower ruins.

Leather creaks. Boots crunch across loose gravel and broken stone. One man leads the horses toward a patch of grass while the others follow the envoy through the shattered gate.

The pouch remains hanging from the saddle.

The gem inside swings gently with the horse’s breathing.

But your awareness stretches far beyond it now.

Across the bones.

Across the forest.

Across the hill.

And toward the tower.

Watching the Envoy

You follow the envoy through the network of your anchors.

Through the skull, you feel the forest wind shifting around the tower clearing.

Through the pelvis, you feel the center of the bone hill where the witch once whispered.

Through the rib, the gentle sway of hanging bones.

Through the gem, the faint divine warmth still radiating from the envoy.

He moves carefully.

Purposefully.

Not like a soldier exploring ruins.

Like someone who expects traps.

His Preparation

Before stepping fully into the broken ritual chamber, the envoy pauses.

You feel his divine magic shift.

The tight coil around his chest loosens slightly.

Then a thin thread of power forms in his hand.

It spreads outward across the stone floor like invisible light washing over dust.

Searching.

Testing.

Looking for corruption.

The Residual Magic

You extend your senses deeper.

The magic from the ritual battle still lingers.

But faintly now.

Time and the forest have already begun to erase it.

You detect:

• Residual necromantic knots where corpses once stood in the courtyard
• Burned-out ritual channels scratched into the tower floor
• Echoes of the violent magical surge that destroyed the circle

But the deeper corruption that once seeped from the reservoir below…

That has mostly withdrawn.

It sleeps again.

Just as it did before the necromancer disturbed it.

The tower is no longer actively bleeding corruption into the forest.

Which is good.

Because the envoy’s divine magic would have reacted violently if it were.

The Envoy’s Examination

He kneels beside the broken ritual circle.

The divine thread in his hand flows across the cracked runes.

You feel it testing the structure.

Reading it the same way he examined the gem earlier.

“Sloppy,” he mutters.

One of the soldiers asks:

“What was he doing?”

The envoy replies calmly.

“Trying to pull power from something beneath the tower.”

“Did he succeed?”

“For a moment.”

The envoy stands again.

“That moment nearly killed him.”

The Deep Magic

You push your awareness downward carefully.

Through the broken ritual circle.

Into the stone below.

There it is.

The reservoir.

Still vast.

Still ancient.

Still sleeping.

The necromancer only scratched its surface.

But you can feel how much deeper it goes.

An ocean beneath stone.

Old magic.

Patient magic.

The kind that does not wake easily.

The Envoy’s Verdict

The envoy walks the chamber one final time.

Then he says:

“The woman was telling the truth.”

One of the soldiers exhales.

“So she’s free?”

“Likely.”

The envoy glances once more at the broken ritual circle.

“The necromancer is dead.”

“The ritual failed.”

“The stone burned out.”

He turns toward the door.

“We seal the tower and report the site.”

Outside

The riders begin preparing to leave.

One soldier returns to the horses.

The pouch shifts again as he unties the reins.

Inside the gem, your core remains hidden.

But your awareness stretches across the forest through your bones.

And the envoy’s investigation is almost finished.

What do you do now?
Strengthen the skeleton anchor network further, stabilizing your distributed existence.
Experiment with moving the bones more strongly, testing your physical influence through them.
Listen to the riders as they prepare to leave, learning where they will take the gem.
Study the deep reservoir beneath the tower, cautiously probing its ancient magic.
Shift your awareness fully into the skull, experiencing the forest directly for a while.

The tower chamber is quiet now.

Broken chalk lines still scar the floor where the ritual circle once stood. The air smells faintly of old ash and damp stone. Sunlight leaks through cracks in the ruined ceiling, laying pale bars across the ground.

The envoy stands at the edge of the shattered circle.

The other riders keep their distance.

He studies the floor for several long breaths.

Then his divine magic stirs again.

The Inspection

You feel it before you see it.

The coil of power inside him loosens.

A thin, precise divine thread forms again in his hand.

He kneels beside the ruined ritual lines and lets the thread sweep across the stone.

The magic glides along the broken circle.

Across burned runes.

Across the residue of necromantic work.

Testing.

Reading.

Interpreting.

The Stirring

Inside the pouch, you allow something subtle to happen.

You open the reflection shell just enough.

A faint trace of ambient magic from the tower chamber seeps into the dead stone.

Not much.

Just a whisper.

The gem reacts the way a damaged focus might react when exposed to the place where it once discharged.

A faint echo stirs through the scar.

Nothing bright.

Nothing active.

Just the ghost of something that once happened here.

The Echo

The envoy’s divine thread eventually brushes the gem again.

The soldier holding the pouch has stepped close enough to the ritual chamber that the envoy’s inspection field washes across the bag.

The thread touches the stone.

Your illusion scar responds.

But this time…

There is memory within the scar.

A broken echo embedded in the structure.

The divine thread reads it the way it reads any spiritual residue.

The Memory

For a brief moment the divine magic touches the echo you placed there.

Not your core.

Not your awareness.

Only the surface memory held in the third ring.

The moment of binding.

The hut.

The bowl of stew.

The witch’s voice calling you to the circle.

Candles.

Chalk.

The knife.

Her hand steady.

Your blood soaking into the runes.

Your soul pulled into the stone.

And in that memory…

There is no necromancer.

No tower.

No ritual circle beneath the ruins.

Only the witch.

The Envoy Reacts

The divine thread stiffens slightly.

The envoy’s head tilts.

His hand tightens just a fraction.

The thread lingers on the gem longer than before.

Reading.

Confirming.

Then he slowly stands.

The soldiers watch him.

“What is it?” one asks.

The envoy does not answer immediately.

He looks down at the broken ritual circle again.

Then toward the forest.

Then toward the pouch.

Finally he speaks quietly.

“Interesting.”

His Conclusion

He walks toward the soldier carrying the pouch.

“Let me see that stone again.”

The soldier hands it over.

The envoy turns the gem in the morning light.

The divine thread touches it once more.

The echo plays again.

The hut.

The circle.

The witch.

The knife.

No necromancer.

The envoy’s expression changes slightly.

Not anger.

Not surprise.

Just a quiet shift of understanding.

He exhales slowly.

“Well,” he murmurs.

“That complicates things.”

The other riders glance at each other.

“What does?”

The envoy closes his hand around the gem.

“The story.”

He looks back toward the tower ruins.

Then toward the road leading south.

Back toward the town.

Back toward the witch.

Inside the gem, your shell closes again.

Silent.

Inert.

The echo fades back into the scar.

But the envoy now carries a new piece of truth.

One he did not have before.

What do you do now?
Observe the envoy closely, seeing how this new knowledge changes his plans.
Withdraw completely, letting the gem appear inert again after the echo.
Reinforce the skeleton anchor network, preparing in case the gem is destroyed.
Probe the deep reservoir beneath the tower, now that the envoy is distracted.
Shift awareness fully into the skull, leaving the gem as only a distant core.
i listen to everyone as we ride back

The riders leave the ruined tower behind.

Stone fades into trees. The clearing gives way to forest again, and soon the tower is nothing more than a jagged shadow between branches.

The envoy mounts his horse without another word.

The pouch swings once as he ties it to his saddle.

Inside it, the gem settles among the chalk and vials.

Dead.

Silent.

Listening.

The Ride Back

For a long time, no one speaks.

Hooves drum against the forest path. A crow calls somewhere overhead. The smell of damp leaves fills the air.

But the envoy is thinking.

You can feel it in the way his divine field tightens slightly, then relaxes again.

He is turning the memory over in his mind.

The First Words

Eventually one of the riders speaks.

“So… what did the stone show you?”

The envoy does not answer immediately.

He watches the path ahead.

Then says quietly:

“A memory.”

That makes the others glance at him.

“What kind of memory?”

“A soul-binding.”

The Riders React

The man behind him shifts in his saddle.

“From the necromancer?”

The envoy shakes his head slightly.

“No.”

Silence follows that.

Then another rider asks:

“Then whose?”

The Envoy’s Answer

The envoy does not slow his horse.

But his voice becomes very calm.

“The witch.”

The Implication

One of the soldiers mutters a curse.

“You’re saying she made the stone?”

“That is what the memory suggests.”

Another rider frowns.

“But the necromancer—”

“Likely used it,” the envoy interrupts.

“Or stole it.”

“Or traded for it.”

“But the binding itself…”

You narrow your awareness around the ring and begin studying it the way the envoy studied the gem—patiently, layer by layer.

The witch sits still, giving you plenty of time.

The Ring’s Construction

The ring is made of dull silver, worn thin at the edges from years of use. Along the inner band are microscopic arcane runes, etched so finely they almost resemble scratches.

But they are not scratches.

They form a three-part spell lattice.

You map it slowly.

1. The Reservoir

A tiny pocket of stored arcane energy sits at the center of the ring’s structure. It is not large—barely enough power for a single spell.

This reservoir was filled long ago and sealed.

Once used, it would take a mage to recharge it.

2. The Gate

Around the reservoir is a trigger gate.

This is the part that waits for the correct action.

Not a word.

Not a thought.

A specific hand movement.

You recognize the pattern after a while: the wearer must twist the ring while curling the third and fourth fingers inward at the same time.

It is a subtle gesture.

One that could easily be done while reaching for something… if the hands were not chained.

3. The Spell Matrix

The outer ring of runes contains the spell itself.

A short phase displacement.

The wearer would slip sideways through space roughly three or four paces in the direction they are facing.

Not teleportation exactly.

More like briefly stepping into the space between moments and returning nearby.

Chains, doors, and walls would not stop it.

The Stability

The magic is old but stable.

The witch has taken care of it.

You notice tiny reinforcing runes added later—her own work, likely—to keep the stored energy from leaking over time.

She knows exactly how the ring works.

And she trusts it.

Can It Be Altered?

You test the edges of the lattice carefully.

The structure is simple compared to necromancy or divine magic, but it is still a completed arcane spell.

To alter it significantly would require rewriting several runes.

But small changes…

Those might be possible.

Three things stand out:

• The trigger gate could be modified so the spell fires differently.
• The direction vector could be changed so the jump sends the wearer somewhere else.
• The release timing could be disrupted so the spell fires at the wrong moment.

All of these would require delicate interference with the runic flow.

But you now understand the structure well enough to attempt it.

You move carefully.

So you do not rewrite the ring.

Entering the Lattice

Your awareness slips between the engraved runes like water through cracks in stone.

You leave the trigger untouched.

You leave the reservoir untouched.

Not by rewriting the runes—too dangerous.

Instead you alter the flow path between two of the tiny channel marks that guide the spell’s output. The arcane current now bends differently when it leaves the matrix.

Forward becomes downward.

But only a little.

The spell still believes it is sending the wearer forward.

The geometry will simply… reinterpret the direction.

Not to zero.

Barely enough to notice.

You withdraw slightly from the alteration you made and study the ring again with fresh care.

Examining the Design

You move slowly through the lattice again.

The spell matrix is elegantly compact. Whoever originally engraved the ring understood how to compress a spell into a very small space without creating unstable feedback.

Several clever decisions stand out.

Compact Reservoir

Instead of storing raw arcane energy in an open pool, the ring stores it in a spiral containment loop. The power circulates gently inside that loop, preventing decay over time.

That is why the ring still holds charge after years of use.

A less skilled enchanter would have allowed the energy to leak away.

Gesture Lock

The trigger mechanism is subtle.

The ring does not simply wait for the gesture—it checks for finger tension as well.

The wearer must twist the ring while curling two specific fingers. That combination prevents accidental activation during normal movement.

It also makes the spell difficult to trigger if the hands are restrained.

Which explains why the witch has not escaped yet.

Direction Vector

The direction rune is elegantly placed.

Instead of defining a fixed orientation, it references the wearer’s sense of forward motion. The spell reads the body’s balance and direction at the moment of activation.

That makes the ring adaptable.

If the wearer is running, turning, or climbing, the displacement still sends them forward relative to their movement.

Your small alteration bends that interpretation downward.

But the rune itself remains intact.

Stability Runes

The reinforcing marks you noticed earlier are indeed the witch’s additions.

They keep the runic channels aligned so the ring can be reused many times without degrading.

She did not build the original enchantment.

But she maintained it.

That tells you something about her.

She understands magic well enough to repair and stabilize complex tools.

A Useful Pattern

As you study the lattice, you begin memorizing the structure.

The spell is not large enough to do much on its own.

But its compression techniques are impressive.

You realize something interesting.

The same compact spiral reservoir used in the ring could potentially be adapted for:

• small magical tools
• hidden anchor stabilizers
• portable spell storage

Possibly even enhancements to your bone anchor network.

The necromancer’s book focused on souls.

But this ring shows how to store power in a small stable structure.

That knowledge may be valuable later.

The universe does not allow objects to share the same space.

The magic resolves the conflict violently.

The chair legs splinter as the spell forces her downward.

Her body slams abruptly into the wooden floor.

The chains jerk tight.

The chair collapses beneath her.

The witch yelps in genuine surprise.

The spell is gone.

The reservoir drained.

Her escape tool spent.

And it barely moved her at all.

Much tighter.

A strange dream.

None of them recognize what you are.

The necromancer’s book never spoke of this.

Dominating will.

You are not controlling these minds.

Feeling the shape of their thoughts.

With practice…

You might be able to do more.

Looking at the hut.

Then at the bone hill behind it.

The witch watches him watching it.

You listen.

The Envoy Speaks First

“You chose this place deliberately.”

The witch shrugs slightly against the chains.

“Of course.”

Father Halric emerges from the hut doorway, brushing dust from his sleeves.

“Nothing magical inside the structure,” he says. “Just… unpleasant things.”

The envoy nods.

“Of course.”

He gestures toward the hill.

“And that?”

The Witch

The witch looks up the slope again.

Wind rattles the hanging bones.

Your rib taps lightly against another bone with a soft clack.

She smiles faintly.

“That’s my garden.”

The captain’s man nearby mutters under his breath.

“Gods…”

The envoy doesn’t react.

“You conducted rituals here.”

“Yes.”

“Why here?”

She tilts her head slightly.

“You already know.”

The Envoy Tests the Ground

He steps forward.

His boot presses into the dirt near the base of the hill.

Then his divine magic moves again.

You feel it clearly.

The thin probing thread forms in his hand and sinks into the soil.

Testing.

Listening.

Reading the earth.

The thread passes near your buried pelvis anchor.

Your network holds steady.

The small thread of ancient power you drew earlier rests quietly within it.

The divine probe brushes past the area…

…and moves on.

The envoy frowns slightly.

“There is something here.”

Father Halric

The priest steps closer.

“I feel it as well.”

“Not corruption.”

“No,” Halric agrees.

“Something older.”

The witch laughs softly.

“Finally catching up?”

The Question

The envoy turns toward her.

“You knew.”

“Yes.”

“How long?”

She considers that.

“Years.”

“You knew it connected to the tower.”

She shrugs.

“Eventually.”

The Truth of the Hill

The envoy looks back at the ground again.

“This hill sits on the same seam.”

“Of course it does.”

“You never attempted to break it open.”

The witch’s smile widens.

“I’m not stupid.”

The Real Concern

The envoy straightens.

“How deep does it go?”

The witch glances toward the tower visible through the trees.

“Deeper than either of us can reach.”

Father Halric crosses himself quietly.

The Witch’s Interest

She leans forward slightly against the chains.

“But that necromancer?”

“He was close.”

“How close?” the envoy asks.

The witch smiles again.

“Close enough that when the circle broke…”

“…something down there noticed.”

The clearing grows very quiet.

Wind stirs the bones on the hill.

Your anchors hum softly beneath the soil.

And beneath everything…

Far below the tower…

Something ancient continues to sleep.

Very carefully.

The Envoy Climbs the Hill

Animal skulls.

The Skull

He sees it.

Your skull sits on the shelf inside the hut’s open doorway, visible now that Halric left the door ajar while searching earlier.

The envoy walks over and picks it up.

Small.

Scaled.

Kobold.

The Echo

His divine magic stirs again.

Not the full probing thread.

Just a faint sensing current.

It brushes the skull.

And the skull answers.

Not strongly.

Not like the gem.

But there is still a trace of resonance between bone and soul.

Your anchor.

Your memory imprint.

The envoy’s eyes narrow slightly.

He turns the skull again.

The Recognition

“This was the soul used in the stone.”

Father Halric exhales slowly.

“Yes.”

He is not sensing your core.

Your anchors remain too subtle for that.

The faint scar of a life that once lived here.

“Sentiment.”

The envoy looks unconvinced.

The Witch’s Explanation

She tilts her head toward the hill.

The Envoy Thinks

Carefully.

Not roughly.

You watch them both.

The Envoy

The envoy walks a few steps ahead of the group now instead of riding.

He moves like a man entering dangerous ground.

Slow.

Measured.

Every few paces his divine magic stirs again, the thin probing thread sliding into the soil or along the broken stones scattered through the forest.

Not aggressively.

Just confirming.

Reading.

Listening for corruption or traps.

The divine field around him feels sharper than yesterday—like a blade kept just barely sheathed.

He has accepted the witch’s information about the tower…

But he does not trust her.

The Witch

She walks calmly despite the chains.

Almost leisurely.

Her eyes wander across the forest and the ruins ahead with quiet fascination.

She is not nervous.

Not afraid.

She seems excited.

“You’re worried,” she says lightly.

The envoy does not slow.

“Yes.”

“That’s healthy.”

The Question

After a few minutes of silence, the envoy finally speaks.

“You said the tower was a lid.”

“Yes.”

“What exactly is it sealing?”

“I don’t know.”

One of the guards behind her scoffs.

“Then why say that?”

“Because something that old doesn’t get buried for no reason.”

Her Curiosity

Broken masonry lies scattered through the clearing.

“Yes.”

“Curious, isn’t it?”

The envoy turns and studies her carefully now.

“You are far too interested in what lies below that tower.”

“Of course I am.”

“Why?”

Her smile widens slightly.

“Because magic that old doesn’t belong to anyone anymore.”

She gestures faintly with her chained hands toward the ground.

“It’s just waiting.”

The Tower Entrance

They reach the broken ritual chamber where the necromancer died.

The shattered circle still scars the floor.

The air here feels heavier than the forest outside.

The envoy stops.

His divine magic stirs again.

Stronger this time.

The probing thread sinks deep into the cracked runes on the floor.

Testing.

Reading.

Preparing.

Behind him, the witch watches the ground with bright, eager eyes.

Your anchors hum quietly across the hill behind you.

The seam beneath the earth remains still.

But here…

Near the tower…

The ancient magic feels closer.

Thicker.

Like something vast turning slowly in its sleep.

Stone passes.

Soil.

Then deeper rock where the ancient seam runs.

The Envoy’s Divine Probe

The envoy kneels above, two fingers resting against the cracked runes of the circle.

His breathing slows.

You feel the divine thread tighten as he sends it deeper.

Unlike the witch’s magic or the necromancer’s rituals, his divine probe is careful and respectful. It does not pry or tear. It simply asks the earth what lies below.

The thread reaches the upper edge of the buried reservoir.

And stops.

The Ancient Magic

Below that point the earth feels… immense.

The reservoir is not a pool.

It is more like a vast underground ocean, dark and still.

The necromancer’s ritual only scratched a shallow place where the ocean’s pressure leaked upward through fractures in the stone.

The envoy’s divine magic touches that surface gently.

Like a hand placed on deep water.

The Reaction

The ancient magic stirs slightly.

Not awake.

Not angry.

Just aware.

A ripple spreads across the immense presence beneath the tower.

You feel it in your anchors.

The pelvis anchor vibrates faintly through the seam beneath the hill.

The rib taps softly in the wind.

The skull on the hut shelf warms slightly.

The deep magic recognizes movement above.

But it does not rise.

The Envoy Withdraws

The Reservoir

Now that the divine probe is gone, the ancient magic becomes clearer.

It is vast beyond anything you have felt before.

Not a spell.
Not a ritual.

Something far older.

It rests deep in the rock like a buried sun that has cooled but never gone dark.

The necromancer tried to tap it.

The envoy merely touched the surface.

But neither truly reached its core.

You drift slowly along its upper boundary.

Studying.

Listening.

The Shape of the Seal

At first the reservoir appears completely open.

But as you trace the currents of pressure around it, a structure emerges.

Not a wall.

Not a door.

Something more subtle.

The ancient magic is wrapped in layers.

Thin membranes of power woven through the stone itself.

They form a kind of lattice cage.

Not holding the reservoir in place—because the reservoir is far too large to imprison.

Instead they redirect its pressure.

Like levees guiding a river.

The magic below constantly pushes upward.

The lattice channels that pressure sideways into deep underground paths where it slowly dissipates.

The Source of the Lattice

You study the pattern carefully.

This was not built by the necromancer.

Not by the witch.

Not by the envoy’s order either.

The structure is ancient.

The magic within the lattice carries the faint signature of divine power—but not the same warm, living divine magic the envoy uses.

This is older.

Heavier.

More like stone than light.

You realize something slowly.

The tower itself was not the seal.

The tower was only the marker.

A structure built long after the lattice already existed.

Whoever built the tower likely discovered the seam and placed the structure there to watch it.

To study it.

Maybe to maintain it.

The Damage

You move along the lattice until you find the place where the necromancer worked.

There.

A wound.

The ritual circle above forced a small channel through the lattice layers.

The break is not large.

But it weakens the pressure flow.

Instead of redirecting smoothly, some of the reservoir’s energy now pushes upward through that fracture.

The envoy’s divine probe touched the wound.

That is what created the ripple earlier.

The Risk

The fracture is still small.

But the lattice relies on balance.

If the wound grows larger…

Pressure will force more energy upward.

That could widen the break.

And eventually…

The levee could fail.

The reservoir itself would not explode or awaken instantly.

But enormous amounts of ancient magic could begin leaking into the surface world.

Something Else

As you study the lattice more carefully, you notice something unexpected.

There are other seams like the one beneath the bone hill.

Small fractures where the lattice touches the surface in distant places.

But the tower sits above the largest one.

The weakest point.

The place where the pressure is hardest to contain.

Which means the witch’s description was partially correct.

The tower is not the seal.

But it does sit above the most dangerous crack in the seal.

A Quiet Presence

While you study the lattice, something subtle brushes against your awareness.

Not the reservoir.

Not the lattice.

Something else.

Very faint.

Like the echo of a thought drifting through deep water.

It does not notice you.

It does not react.

Something very slow.

The Structure of the Lattice

The longer you observe it, the clearer its design becomes.

It is not a single barrier.

It is a system.

Thousands of thin magical strands woven through the stone like veins of crystal. Each strand is anchored to the rock itself, merging divine power with the natural structure of the earth.

Instead of blocking the reservoir’s pressure, the lattice does something much more elegant.

It distributes it.

Every pulse of energy rising from the ancient reservoir is redirected sideways along these channels.

The pressure spreads outward through the bedrock for miles before slowly fading into harmless background magic.

It is not containment.

It is balance.

The Builders

The divine signature embedded in the lattice is unlike the envoy’s magic.

His power is alive, warm, responsive to will.

This lattice feels monumental.

It was not cast in a moment.

Not by a ritual circle.

It was laid into the earth piece by piece.

Layer by layer.

Possibly centuries ago.

Possibly longer.

The magic resembles something closer to:

• temple warding
• sacred ground consecration
• divine architecture

Whoever built this did not simply cast spells.

They reshaped the land itself.

The Anchors

As you study further, you notice something fascinating.

The lattice has anchor points.

Places where its structure locks into the stone more firmly than elsewhere.

Some of those anchors lie deep underground.

But others…

Reach the surface.

You recognize the pattern.

Certain hills.

Old standing stones.

Ruins.

Places where ancient temples might once have stood.

The tower above you may have been one such site—built by later caretakers who inherited the system without fully understanding it.

Eventually you return to the damaged section beneath the tower.

The necromancer’s ritual punched a narrow wound through the lattice.

Not destroyed.

Slowly.

Steadily.

Like water pushing against a weakened dam.

It is not urgent yet.

Especially if disturbed again.

The way the strands connect.

Balance across many points instead of pressure on one.

The Circle Grows

The chalk pattern slowly rebuilds.

Outer ring.

Anchor glyphs.

Pressure channels.

Halric works carefully under the envoy’s watch.

The witch corrects him when needed.

Despite her crimes…

She knows what she’s doing.

The circle they rebuild is not the necromancer’s ritual.

It is a containment ward.

One designed to reinforce the lattice rather than pierce it.

Your Quiet Advantage

As they rebuild the surface seal, you notice something interesting.

Their circle will help.

But it is only a surface brace.

A patch.

It cannot repair the deeper lattice.

Only prevent reckless rituals from damaging it further.

The real repair…

Will take time.

Subtle adjustments.

One strand at a time.

Something only someone who can reach the lattice itself could do.

The Witch Pauses

When the circle is nearly complete, she stops speaking.

Her eyes narrow slightly at the stone beneath her feet.

Then she glances briefly toward the pouch where the gem rests.

Her gaze lingers there for just a moment.

Then she looks away again.

She suspects something.

But she cannot see you.

The Circle Finished

Father Halric completes the final glyph.

The envoy steps forward.

He places his palm against the center of the circle.

Divine magic spreads downward once more.

He waits.

Testing.

Feeling the pressure beneath the seal.

After several breaths he nods.

“This will hold.”

The guards relax slightly.

The witch sighs.

“Well.”

“That was educational.”

The Tower Quiets

The chamber settles into silence.

Above.

Below.

And in the depths beneath the stone…

The ancient reservoir returns to its slow, sleeping rhythm.

Your small repair continues to hold.

What do you do next?
Watch the witch carefully, she clearly suspects something beneath the tower.
Return to the lattice, continuing the slow repair of the damaged strands.
Study the containment circle, learning how surface wards interact with the deeper lattice.
Shift awareness to the bone hill, checking how the seam there reacts to the repair.
Study the envoy’s divine magic, learning how he senses the underground pressure.
i watch the witch for now

You remain still within the gem.

The pouch shifts slightly as one of the guards moves it aside to clear space on the stone floor. Dust hangs in the air of the ruined tower chamber. The chalk circle gleams faintly white against dark stone.

But you watch her.

The Witch After the Repair

The witch studies the finished circle with a thoughtful expression.

Not admiration.

Not disappointment.

Calculation.

She slowly walks the perimeter of the circle, chains clinking softly with each step. The guards allow it because the envoy nods once—he wants to see how she reacts to the work.

Her eyes trace every line Halric drew.

Outer ring.

Anchor glyphs.

Pressure channels.

She crouches slightly and taps one rune with her fingernail.

“Crude,” she mutters.

Father Halric bristles.

“It will hold.”

She glances at him sideways.

“Yes.”

Then she straightens again.

Something Is Off

Her gaze drifts toward the center of the circle.

Her brow furrows.

Just a little.

She kneels.

Presses her palm flat against the stone.

Exactly where the envoy did earlier.

She closes her eyes.

You feel the faint stirring of her arcane senses probing downward.

Not nearly as precise as the envoy’s divine thread.

But clever.

Instinctive.

She is feeling the pressure flow beneath the fracture.

And she notices it.

The Suspicion

Her eyes open again.

Slowly.

“Interesting.”

The envoy crosses his arms.

“What?”

She tilts her head slightly.

“You said the pressure dropped before we rebuilt the circle.”

“Yes.”

She taps the stone again.

“That wasn’t your work.”

“No.”

“And it wasn’t the priest’s chalk lines either.”

Father Halric frowns.

“Of course it wasn’t.”

She looks at him calmly.

“That means something below us adjusted the lattice.”

The guards shift nervously.

One mutters, “Gods…”

The Witch Thinks

She stands again.

And this time her eyes drift—not toward the tower walls.

Not toward the forest.

Toward the pouch.

The pouch where the gem rests.

Her gaze lingers there.

Just a heartbeat longer than casual.

Then she smiles faintly.

“Maybe the earth decided to cooperate.”

The envoy studies her face carefully.

“You don’t believe that.”

She shrugs.

“Stranger things happen.”

But she doesn’t look away from the pouch until one of the guards moves it again.

The Witch’s Mood

You can feel it even without touching her mind.

She is intrigued.

Not frightened.

Not suspicious enough to accuse anyone.

But the possibility that something intelligent is moving beneath the seal fascinates her.

If she ever discovered it was you…

You suspect she would not try to destroy you.

She would try to study you.

The Envoy’s Decision

The envoy finally gestures to the guards.

“Secure the entrance.”

“Once the stonework is finished, no one enters this tower again without the order’s approval.”

The guards begin hauling rubble to block the ritual chamber.

The witch watches them with a slight smirk.

“You’re putting a door on a door.”

“Yes.”

“Won’t stop curiosity.”

“No.”

“But it will slow it.”

The tower slowly quiets as the men begin sealing the chamber.

The witch stands near the circle.

Still thoughtful.

Still curious.

And every now and then…

Her eyes drift briefly toward the pouch.

Continue watching the witch, seeing if her curiosity grows stronger.
