You remain quiet inside the gem while the chamber changes around you.

Stone scrapes against stone as the guards drag fallen blocks toward the ritual entrance. Dust rises in pale clouds. The half-rebuilt tower echoes with the dull grind of masonry.

The witch stands off to one side, chains loose enough for her to walk but still held by a guard.

You listen.

The Envoy’s Orders

The envoy brushes chalk dust from his gloves.

“This chamber gets sealed.”

One of the soldiers nods. “For good?”

“For now.”

Father Halric glances uneasily toward the circle.

“And the lattice below?”

“The surface brace will hold,” the envoy replies. “At least long enough for the order to send proper wardens.”

The witch chuckles softly.

“Wardens.”

What Comes Next

Halric lowers his voice slightly.

“And the woman?”

The guards glance toward her.

The envoy does not hesitate.

“She returns with us.”

“To the capital?”

“Yes.”

Halric exhales.

“The bishop will want to hear this himself.”

The witch tilts her head.

“Oh good.”

“New audience.”

The Charge

One guard clears his throat.

“What exactly are we telling them?”

The envoy answers calmly.

“That she murdered a child and bound its soul.”

“That she assisted in stopping a necromancer.”

“And that she helped stabilize an ancient seal beneath this tower.”

The guard looks uneasy.

“That sounds complicated.”

“It is.”

The Witch’s Reaction

She laughs quietly.

“You’re presenting me as a criminal and a consultant.”

The envoy looks at her without humor.

“You are both.”

She nods slightly.

“Fair.”

The Real Reason

Father Halric glances toward the sealed circle again.

“You’re not sending her back because she helped.”

The envoy shakes his head.

“No.”

“Then why?”

The envoy looks toward the ground beneath the tower.

“Because she understands this place.”

“And if the seal ever fails…”

“…she may be one of the few people alive who knows how to deal with it.”

The witch’s smile widens.

“See? I told you I’d be useful.”

The Journey Ahead

The guards finish stacking the last stones across the chamber entrance.

The envoy nods once.

“That’s enough.”

“We ride back to town.”

“Then the capital.”

The witch sighs theatrically.

“Long trip in chains.”

The envoy turns away.

“Get used to it.”

A Quiet Moment

As the others begin gathering their gear, the witch pauses beside the pouch.

Just briefly.

Her fingers brush the leather.

Not opening it.

Just touching it.

Her eyes flick toward the gem inside.

Then she looks away again and walks after the guards.

The tower begins to empty.

Soon the chamber will fall silent again.

But now you know the next path the story will take:

The capital.

And the witch will travel there under guard.

What do you do before they leave the tower?
Watch the witch closely, her curiosity about the gem hasn’t gone away.
Return to the lattice, making one more quiet adjustment before the tower is sealed.

i shift to the bones and study the hill to see how things are there

You let the stone chamber fade again.

The chalk circle.
The guards hauling rubble.
The witch brushing the pouch.

All of it slips away as you follow the familiar threads of your anchors outward.

Gem → Pelvis → Rib → Skull → Femur

Your awareness spreads across them like wind through branches.

Then settles into the hill.

The Bone Hill

The forest is quiet here.

Wind pushes through tall grass behind the hut. The hanging bones clack softly together. A crow lands briefly on the crooked fence before hopping away again.

Nothing living has disturbed the place.

But beneath the surface…

The hill feels different.

The Seam After the Repair

You sink into the soil again.

Past the roots.

Past the fragments of old bones.

Down to the seam where the ancient lattice brushes the surface.

The thread of power you borrowed earlier is still resting in the pelvis anchor.

Not draining.

Not growing.

Just stabilizing the structure of your network.

And the seam itself…

Is calmer.

Pressure Flow

Before, the seam hummed faintly with upward pressure from the reservoir.

Now that you nudged one strand of the lattice back into place, that pressure has shifted.

Less magic is pushing upward through the fracture beneath the tower.

Which means less strain travels along the branch reaching this hill.

The entire seam here feels steadier.

Your anchors respond to it.

The rib sways in the wind with a slightly stronger resonance.

The pelvis anchor holds the network like a keystone.

Even the skull in the hut feels clearer—your awareness moves between anchors with less resistance.

Your small repair below the tower has strengthened this place too.

The Bones

You listen to the hill again.

The bones whisper faint impressions.

Old deaths.

Old rituals.

But the whispers are quieter now.

Less agitation.

As if the earth itself is relaxing after a long tension.

You realize something subtle:

The witch likely felt this change too.

She lived here long enough to notice when the hill’s magic shifts.

That is probably why she became suspicious earlier.

The Forest Around the Hill

You extend your senses outward through the anchors.

The hut remains abandoned.

No travelers.

No animals larger than a fox moving through the brush.

The forest feels ordinary again.

No rising corruption.

No pressure from below.

For now…

The ancient reservoir is sleeping peacefully.

A New Awareness

While studying the hill, you begin noticing something else about your anchor network.

The seam beneath the hill does not just stabilize the anchors.

It acts almost like a natural amplifier.

Small movements of awareness flow more easily through the bones here than anywhere else.

If the gem were ever lost…

Or destroyed…

This hill might become the true center of your existence.

Hooves in the Distance

Through the skull in the hut you faintly hear movement again.

The riders are leaving the tower.

Returning toward the hut clearing.

Soon they will pass through this place again before heading back toward the town.

And eventually…

Toward the capital.

What do you do now?
Remain at the hill, studying how the seam strengthens your anchor network.
Experiment with moving the bones, testing how much physical influence you have here.
Return to the gem, observing the witch and envoy during the ride back.
Explore further along the seam, mapping where this branch of the lattice leads.

You let your awareness drift outward from the bones.

The forest around the hill is alive with small presences—simple minds moving through instinct and hunger.

You find one easily.

The Fox

A small red fox moves quietly along the edge of the clearing.

Its nose stays low to the ground, sniffing between fallen leaves. The animal is cautious, ears twitching at every sound.

You reach out gently.

Not pushing.

Just brushing the surface of its mind the way you brushed the dreams of the townsfolk earlier.

The Fox’s Mind

The difference is immediate.

Human thoughts are layered.

Memories, language, plans.

The fox has none of that.

Its mind is a map of sensations.

Smell.

Movement.

Hunger.

Cold.

The rustle of something beneath leaves.

You step lightly into that stream of instinct.

The fox pauses.

Its ears flick once.

Its head lifts slightly.

It cannot understand what you are.

But it feels something unfamiliar brushing its awareness.

The Shared Moment

For a brief instant you see the world through the fox.

The forest is a tapestry of scents:

• mice under roots
• damp bark
• the faint smell of humans near the hut
• the lingering scent of the witch herself

The fox’s heartbeat quickens slightly as it senses the humans returning through the trees.

You feel its instinct:

Avoid.

Watch.

Wait.

There is no fear of you specifically.

Just the unease of something unknown.

A Small Influence

You test something gently.

Not control.

Just a suggestion.

Stay.

The fox pauses where it stands instead of fleeing immediately.

It lowers itself into the grass, watching the clearing carefully.

Your presence rests lightly beside its instincts.

Not directing.

Just sharing.

The Riders Return

Through the fox’s sharp hearing you catch the sound of hooves and metal long before they reach the clearing.

The envoy and his riders approach the hut again.

The witch among them.

The fox watches silently from the brush.

And through its senses…

So do you.

What do you do now?
Remain linked with the fox, using its senses to observe the riders unnoticed.
Experiment with guiding the fox, seeing how much influence you truly have.
Withdraw from the fox’s mind, returning to your anchors before the connection deepens too much.
Listen to the riders through the fox’s vantage, learning what they say on the ride back.
Touch another nearby animal, comparing different kinds of minds.
i give the fox a 'pet' and then let it go, returning to the stone

You rest beside the fox for one quiet moment.

The small creature remains crouched in the grass, ears twitching as the distant riders approach the hut clearing.

You let your awareness brush its mind one last time.

Not a command.

Not a push.

Just something gentle.

The closest thing your strange, disembodied presence can manage to a pet behind the ears.

For an instant the fox relaxes. Its tail flicks once in the grass. It doesn’t understand the sensation—only that the strange pressure that brushed its mind feels calm rather than threatening.

Then you withdraw.

The fox’s instincts immediately return to the front of its thoughts.

Humans nearby.

Noise.

Danger.

It slips quietly into the brush and disappears between the roots of the trees.

Returning to the Gem

You follow the threads of your anchors back.

Fox → Forest → Bones → Hill → Pelvis → Gem.

The shift is smooth now.

The pouch’s darkness returns.

Leather creaks softly with the movement of the envoy’s horse.

Outside, voices drift faintly through the fabric.

The Riders at the Hut

The group has paused briefly in the clearing.

One of the guards speaks.

“Strange place to live.”

The witch shrugs slightly.

“Cheap land.”

Another guard mutters as he looks up the bone hill.

“Looks cursed.”

The witch smirks.

“Everything is cursed if you wait long enough.”

The envoy doesn’t respond.

He glances once toward the hut door.

Then toward the hill.

His divine senses brush the ground again.

Briefly.

Testing.

The lattice holds steady beneath the earth.

Your adjustment remains unnoticed.

Departure

“Mount up,” the envoy finally says.

“We return to town before nightfall.”

The guards pull the witch back onto her horse.

Chains clink.

The pouch shifts again as the gem swings gently from the envoy’s saddle.

Soon the clearing begins to fade behind them as the riders head south.

Back toward the town.

And eventually…

Toward the capital.

The road south is quiet except for hooves and the creak of leather.

The forest slowly thins as the riders move away from the tower and the strange hill behind it. Sunlight filters through branches overhead, warming the damp air of the path.

Inside the pouch, the gem rests among the witch’s confiscated tools.

You listen.

The Guards Talk

At first the guards ride in silence.

Then one of the men behind the witch clears his throat.

“You ever heard of something like that before?”

The rider beside him snorts.

“Ancient magic under a tower?”

“Yeah.”

“No.”

The Capital

Another guard farther back joins in.

“The order’s dealt with worse.”

“How would you know?”

“My cousin’s in the city watch in the capital.”

“What did he say?”

The guard lowers his voice slightly.

“Temple district’s full of strange stuff. Old relic vaults. Buried shrines under the cathedral.”

The other rider frowns.

“And they just keep that stuff there?”

“Better there than loose in the countryside.”

The Witch’s Reputation

One of the men glances toward the witch riding ahead.

“Still don’t like traveling with her.”

The other shrugs.

“She’s in chains.”

“Doesn’t matter.”

“Why?”

“She smiles too much.”

The second guard chuckles.

“Yeah.”

The Capital’s Order

The conversation drifts again after a while.

“You think the bishop’s really going to question her himself?”

The guard beside him nods.

“If the envoy says the tower’s real, yeah.”

“Why?”

“Because if something under that tower wakes up…”

“…the order’s the only group big enough to deal with it.”

Another rider mutters quietly.

“Let’s hope it stays asleep.”

The Witch Interrupts

The witch tilts her head slightly.

“You boys talk like I summoned a demon.”

The guard beside her scowls.

“You killed a kid.”

She shrugs.

“Yes.”

“That part’s settled.”

The guard grips his reins tighter but doesn’t reply.

The envoy glances back briefly but says nothing.

The Road Continues

The forest thins further as they approach farmland again.

The town’s outer fields are only a few hours away now.

Eventually the conversation fades into quiet riding again.

But you’ve learned something useful.

The capital isn’t just a city.

It’s where the order keeps its deeper knowledge.

Old relics.

Buried shrines.

Ancient vaults.

Places where things like the tower’s reservoir are studied… or contained.

And that is where the witch is being taken.

The road stretches long toward the capital.

Fields replace forest. Small farms appear along the roadside—low stone walls, wheat bending in the wind, smoke rising from cookfires. Travelers occasionally pass the column and quickly step aside when they see the envoy’s crest.

The witch rides at the center of it all.

And you watch her.

The Witch on the Road

She sits comfortably in the saddle despite the chains.

Not slumped like a prisoner.

Balanced.

Alert.

Her eyes roam constantly.

Sometimes the road.

Sometimes the distant hills.

Sometimes the envoy riding ahead.

But every so often…

Her gaze drifts toward the pouch hanging from the envoy’s saddle.

Toward you.

Not directly.

Not staring.

Just… noticing.

Her Thoughts

You don’t push into her mind.

But you’ve touched enough minds now to feel the shape of it from the outside.

The witch’s thoughts are nothing like the sleepy guards or the dreaming child.

Her mind is sharp.

Layered.

Full of small calculations.

Every sound.

Every movement.

Every guard position.

She studies it all automatically.

But one thought keeps returning.

Something changed the pressure below the tower.

She rolls that idea over again and again.

Her Curiosity

After several hours of riding she finally speaks again.

Not to the guards.

To the envoy.

“You really didn’t move the lattice?”

“No.”

“Nor the priest?”

“No.”

“Then we’ve got a mystery.”

“Possibly.”

The Witch’s Theory

She leans forward slightly in the saddle.

“There are old stories, you know.”

The envoy doesn’t respond.

“Places where the earth itself wakes up.”

“Places where the magic under the world pushes back.”

Still nothing from him.

She chuckles softly.

“Or maybe someone down there doesn’t like being disturbed.”

One of the guards mutters under his breath.

“Don’t start that again.”

The Envoy’s Silence

The envoy never rises to the bait.

But you notice something.

When she says someone down there…

His divine field tightens slightly.

Not fear.

But awareness.

He felt the ripple too.

He simply refuses to speculate aloud.

The Witch Looks Back

Later in the afternoon the witch glances behind the group.

Toward the distant forest where the tower stands hidden beyond the hills.

Her voice drops slightly.

“You know…”

“…if something did fix the lattice…”

“Don’t.”

By sunset the walls of a larger town appear ahead.

This is not the capital yet—just a stop along the road.

But the towers of the city lie somewhere beyond the horizon.

The witch sits quietly now as they approach the gate.

Still curious.

Still thinking.

And every now and then…

Her eyes flick back toward the pouch again.

As the riders approach the roadside town, the column slows. Hooves clop more softly on packed dirt, and the smell of livestock and cooking fires drifts across the evening air.

You reach outward again.

Not toward a human mind this time.

Toward the horse carrying the pouch.

Entering the Horse’s Mind

You brush against the animal gently.

Immediately the world changes.

Where the fox’s mind was sharp and quick, the horse’s mind is broad and steady—like a slow river rather than a rushing stream.

The first things you feel are not thoughts but sensations:

• the pull of the reins against its bit
• the steady rhythm of hooves striking earth
• the weight of saddle and rider
• the warm scent of the other horses nearby

The horse’s mind doesn’t organize things into words or plans.

It knows comfort, direction, and herd.

And it knows the rider on its back.

The Rider’s Presence

Through the horse’s senses you feel the envoy.

Not his divine magic directly—but his presence.

The horse knows him as:

steady hands
clear commands
not cruel

Animals notice those things more clearly than humans do.

This horse trusts him.

The Road Through the Horse

Your senses widen through the animal.

You feel the entire group as the horse does:

• the witch’s horse slightly behind and to the left
• the guard riding close to her
• the shifting tension in the herd when the witch laughs
• the smell of the town ahead

The horse notices the witch too.

Not as a criminal.

Not as a threat.

Just as a rider whose horse smells restless and tense.

Animals read the body more than the mind.

The witch’s horse feels her alertness through the reins and posture.

Testing Influence

You try a small suggestion again.

Nothing strong.

Just the same gentle push you gave the fox.

Easy.

The horse exhales through its nose.

Its gait relaxes slightly.

The envoy barely notices the change except for a light adjustment of the reins.

You are not controlling the animal.

Just smoothing its instincts.

The Witch’s Horse

Your awareness brushes the horse carrying the witch as well.

That animal feels different.

Tense.

Its muscles carry the constant small pressure of a rider who is always adjusting balance, always ready to move.

The witch may look relaxed…

But her body never fully settles.

Her horse knows it.

The column finally reaches the small town’s gate.

Guards step aside quickly when they recognize the envoy.

The horses slow to a walk as they pass into the street.

Lanterns flicker along the road.

The smell of stew and bread fills the air.

The horse’s mind relaxes slightly now that the day’s ride is ending.

And through its senses…

You watch the witch as well.

You release the horse’s mind gently.

The steady rhythm of hooves fades, along with the animal’s simple awareness of road, herd, and rider. The sensation slips away like a tide pulling back from shore.

Your awareness flows back along the familiar threads:

Horse → Road → Saddle → Pouch → Gem.

Darkness surrounds you again inside the leather pouch.

But your senses stretch outward through the thin openings in the fabric, and through the faint magical awareness you’ve learned to extend.

Entering the Town

The riders pass through the town gate.

Lanterns glow along the main road, their yellow light reflecting off damp cobblestones. People pause in doorways or step aside with curious looks as the small escort passes.

This place is larger than the farms you passed earlier, but still small compared to the capital.

A roadside town.

Travelers’ inns.

A stable yard.

A smithy still glowing faintly from the forge.

The sounds are lively compared to the quiet countryside.

• carts rumbling
• people talking over evening meals
• dogs barking from fenced yards
• a fiddle playing somewhere down the street

The Witch’s Reaction

The witch watches everything.

Her eyes move constantly from doorway to alley to rooftop.

She counts the guards at the gate without turning her head.

She notes the stables.

The inn.

The alleyways.

Not planning an escape right now—but mapping the terrain the way a predator studies a hunting ground.

Her curiosity about the gem and the tower hasn’t faded, but survival still comes first.

The Envoy

The envoy leads them straight through the main street.

He does not stop at the tavern or inn.

Instead he guides the riders toward a small stone building near the far side of town.

A shrine.

The symbol above the doorway matches the one on his cloak.

This is an outpost of the order.

A place where traveling templars and priests can rest under the church’s authority.

The guards at the door straighten immediately when they see him.

The Stop for the Night

The horses are led toward the stable behind the shrine.

The witch is dismounted and handed down to the ground.

Chains clink again as the guards guide her inside.

The pouch containing the gem is carried with the envoy into the building.

Lantern light fills the entry hall.

Stone walls.

Prayer alcoves.

A long wooden table where travelers’ gear is set down.

The gem is placed there among the witch’s confiscated belongings.

The Town at Night

Outside the shrine the town continues its evening rhythm.

Laughter from a nearby tavern.

Farmers finishing their meals.

Travelers passing through on the road.

Inside the shrine, though, things quiet quickly.

The witch is placed in a small locked chamber.

Two guards remain outside the door.

The envoy and Father Halric speak quietly in another room.

Night is settling in.

What do you do while the group settles for the night?
Watch the witch in her chamber, seeing how she behaves when alone again.
Listen to the envoy and Father Halric, learning more about the order and the capital.
Drift through the town, exploring new minds and dreams as people fall asleep.

Here is a Session Summary designed to preserve the important state of the world, your abilities, and narrative threads while reducing token load for future continuation.

SESSION SUMMARY
Player Character

Identity:
Young male kobold whose body was sacrificed by a witch and soul bound into a gem.

Current Soul Anchors:

Primary Core

Soul bound within small black gem carried by the envoy.

Secondary Anchors (Skeleton Network)

Skull inside the witch’s hut.
Pelvis buried in the bone hill.
Rib hanging on the bone hill.
Femur inside hollow tree near hill.

Network Characteristics

Anchors distribute soul stability similar to a skeletal framework.
Pelvis acts as central stabilizing node.
Gem remains the primary core, but the hill seam may eventually support independence if the gem is lost.

i listen to the envoy and halric

Night settles over the shrine.

Outside, the town has quieted to low voices and the occasional bark of a dog. Wind moves softly against the stone walls. Lanternlight flickers through narrow windows.

Inside the shrine, most of the guards have gone to the common room to eat.

But the envoy and Father Halric remain awake.

They sit at the long wooden table where the confiscated items rest.

The pouch with the gem lies only a few inches from Halric’s elbow.

You listen.

The Envoy Speaks

“The tower isn’t the real problem.”

Halric folds his hands.

“No. The thing beneath it is.”

The envoy nods once.

“What concerns me is the age of the lattice.”

Halric frowns.

“You think it predates the order?”

“I’m certain of it.”

The Lattice

Halric glances down at the table as if imagining the earth beneath it.

“That kind of divine architecture… I’ve only seen references to it in cathedral foundations.”

The envoy leans back slightly.

“Which means whoever built it had resources greater than ours.”

Halric goes quiet for a moment.

“That’s not comforting.”

“No.”

The Fracture

Halric rubs his temples.

“The necromancer nearly broke it.”

“Yes.”

“And the pressure dropped before we rebuilt the circle.”

“Yes.”

Halric hesitates.

“Do you believe the witch?”

“That something down there moved?”

The envoy is silent for several seconds.

Finally he says:

“No.”

Halric exhales in relief.

“Good.”

But…

The envoy’s voice continues quietly.

“I believe something changed the lattice.”

Halric’s relief fades immediately.

“That’s worse.”

“Yes.”

The Possibility

Halric lowers his voice.

“Could it be an old guardian?”

The envoy shakes his head.

“If something that powerful still existed, the tower would never have weakened.”

Halric glances toward the witch’s cell down the hall.

“So what do you think it was?”

The envoy rests his hand lightly on the pouch.

You feel the leather press against the gem.

His divine magic brushes the pouch briefly.

Just a faint scan.

Not strong enough to penetrate your disguise.

“I don’t know,” he says.

The Witch

Halric shifts the subject.

“What will the bishop do with her?”

The envoy’s voice is flat.

“Question her.”

“And after that?”

“If she’s lying about the tower, she hangs.”

Halric nods slowly.

“And if she isn’t?”

The envoy looks toward the floor again.

“Then we may need her.”

The Capital

Halric sighs.

“I hope the cathedral archives still have records about that lattice.”

The envoy stands.

“They will.”

“And if they don’t?”

The envoy pauses at the doorway.

“Then we start digging.”

The two men leave the room soon after.

The pouch with the gem remains on the table in the quiet shrine.

Down the hall, the witch’s cell is silent.

But somewhere in the building…

You can feel her mind still awake.

Thinking.

What do you do now?
Visit the witch’s dreams, see what occupies her mind tonight.
Explore the shrine, sensing any wards or relics kept here.
Drift through the town, entering the dreams of the sleeping villagers.
Study your anchor network, strengthening the stability between bones and gem.
Return briefly to the bone hill, checking the seam after the tower repair.
i explore the shrine

The shrine settles into the deep quiet of night.

Lanterns burn low in iron brackets along the stone walls. Their light leaves long shadows across the floor, and the smell of old incense lingers in the air.

The pouch sits unattended on the long table.

From within the gem, you extend your awareness outward.

Slowly.

Carefully.

The Shrine

The building is small but solid.

Stone foundation. Thick walls. Wooden beams above. It was built more for durability than beauty—one of the roadside sanctuaries used by the order while traveling between cities.

But despite its size, the place carries layers of old devotion.

You feel it immediately.

The Wards

Not traps.

Not aggressive magic.

These are sanctified boundaries.

Thin threads of divine energy run through the stone foundation and the doorframes, like faint veins beneath skin.

Their purpose is simple:

• discourage restless spirits
• weaken necromantic workings
• warn priests of corruption

They are not meant to imprison something like you.

But they make the space feel heavy.

Warm.

Bright.

A place built to comfort the living and deny the dead.

Your presence slips through them carefully.

Your disguise as a burned-out soul stone helps.

The wards brush against you but do not react.

The Prayer Hall

You drift through the main chamber.

Simple wooden pews face a stone altar carved with the symbol of the order.

Above it hangs a small relic lantern.

Inside the lantern burns a steady blue-white flame.

This flame is not ordinary fire.

It is a minor divine relic.

Its purpose is to keep the shrine’s sanctification active even when no priest is present.

You feel the warmth of its power clearly.

It would be uncomfortable to linger too close for long.

But it does not detect you.

The Guest Cells

Beyond the prayer hall are several small sleeping chambers.

Traveling priests use them when passing through.

One room holds Father Halric.

He sleeps lightly.

His dreams drift through quiet prayers and fragments of scripture.

Another room holds two guards.

They snore loudly.

Their dreams are dull and heavy.

The Witch

At the end of the hallway lies the locked chamber where the witch is kept.

Two guards sit outside the door.

One nodding off.

The other slowly sharpening a dagger.

Inside the room…

The witch is not sleeping.

She sits on the narrow cot with her back against the wall.

Eyes open.

Watching the dark.

Thinking.

Something Interesting

As you drift through the shrine, you notice something else.

Beneath the altar stone…

There is a small buried object.

A reliquary.

Old.

Probably placed there when the shrine was built.

It radiates faint divine energy, much older than the lantern flame.

This object is likely the true anchor that sanctifies the entire building.

The lantern simply feeds it.

The Night

The shrine is calm.

Protected.

Sacred.

But none of its wards suspect that a soul bound in a gem now quietly explores its halls.

And down the corridor…

The witch still sits awake.

Thinking about the tower.

And the mystery beneath it.

What do you do?
Study the buried reliquary, learning how the shrine’s sanctification works.
Visit the witch’s mind, carefully brushing the edge of her thoughts.
Observe the divine lantern, studying how relic magic sustains the shrine.
Drift outside the shrine, exploring the sleeping town around it.
Return to the gem, preparing for whatever happens when the journey continues.
i study the reliquary

You drift beneath the altar.

The stone slab above you is thick and old, worn smooth by decades of prayer and kneeling pilgrims. The lantern’s pale flame casts soft light across its carved surface, but the object you are searching for lies under it.

You sink through the stone slowly.

Carefully.

The Reliquary

Beneath the altar, set into a hollow in the foundation stone, rests a small iron coffer.

It is no larger than a human hand.

The metal is dark with age but engraved with fine lines that form a protective sigil—a simple but enduring divine ward.

Inside the coffer rests the source of the shrine’s sanctification.

A fragment of bone.

Human.

A finger bone, polished smooth with age.

The Saint’s Fragment

The bone is wrapped in thin strips of linen, now yellowed with time.

The moment your awareness brushes near it, you feel a steady radiance spreading through the stone around it.

Not blazing power.

Not forceful magic.

But something constant.

Like sunlight that never fades.

This is the relic of a saint or martyr—someone whose life and death became sacred enough that their remains still carry divine resonance.

How It Works

You study the structure around it.

The reliquary is not meant to cast spells.

It simply exists.

The shrine’s architecture channels its presence.

Stone lines etched beneath the altar guide the relic’s aura outward through the floor, the walls, and the doorway thresholds.

The lantern above the altar feeds a small amount of divine energy into the system to keep it active.

Together they create a field that:

• discourages undead
• weakens necromancy
• comforts the living
• alerts priests if corruption enters

It is elegant.

Simple.

Durable.

Very different from arcane magic.

The Effect on You

Your soul does not recoil from it.

But the relic’s presence is… uncomfortable.

Not hostile.

Just clarifying.

Your anchor network feels sharper near it, like standing in cold water.

If you linger here too long, the divine resonance might begin examining you more closely.

Your disguise as a burned-out soul stone helps, but the relic is older and subtler than the lantern’s magic.

A Strange Insight

As you study it, you notice something unexpected.

The relic’s aura behaves very much like the lattice beneath the tower.

Not in scale.

But in principle.

It does not contain power.

It radiates stability outward into the structure around it.

A node.

An anchor.

A stabilizing point.

Very much like your pelvis anchor in the bone hill.

Very much like the lattice anchor sites beneath the earth.

The Quiet Shrine

Above you, the shrine remains silent.

The guards murmur softly in the hallway.

Father Halric shifts in his sleep.

And down the corridor…

The witch is still awake.

Her thoughts moving quietly in the dark.

What do you do next?
Study the relic’s aura more deeply, learning how divine anchors radiate stability.
Compare the reliquary to your anchor network, refining your own structure.
Visit the witch’s mind, seeing what keeps her awake tonight.
Examine the lantern above the altar, studying how it feeds the shrine’s wards.
Withdraw from the reliquary, before its divine resonance begins probing you.
i examine the lantern above

You withdraw from the reliquary before its quiet radiance can study you too closely.

Rising back through the altar stone, your awareness emerges into the prayer hall again.

Above the altar hangs the lantern.

You drift closer.

The Lantern

It hangs from a simple iron hook.

Glass panes surround the flame inside, though the fire itself burns with a pale blue-white glow instead of orange.

This is not normal fire.

It is consecrated flame.

A small divine construct maintained through ritual rather than fuel.

You move closer, studying the structure.

The Flame

Unlike arcane enchantments, the lantern contains no runes.

No spell matrix.

Instead, the flame itself is bound through prayer structure.

Halric or another priest likely renews it periodically with a short ritual.

The flame feeds divine resonance into the shrine’s foundation.

You can feel the flow clearly:

Lantern → altar stone → reliquary → etched foundation lines → shrine walls.

The lantern is essentially a pump.

It feeds energy into the relic so the relic’s aura spreads through the shrine continuously.

Without the lantern, the reliquary would still work…

But far more slowly.

Studying the Flame

You extend your awareness into the flame’s edge.

Carefully.

The divine energy here feels warmer than the relic below.

More alive.

More responsive.

You experiment slightly, shaping a tiny thread of divine energy like the envoy did earlier.

The flame reacts.

Not aggressively.

But curiously.

The thread you shape blends briefly with the lantern’s aura before dispersing.

An Important Realization

Divine magic here behaves differently from arcane magic.

Arcane magic follows structure.

Divine magic follows intention.

The lantern continues burning because generations of priests have reinforced the idea that this flame should exist.

Faith made permanent.

A Small Possibility

You realize something interesting.

Your divine manipulation—still weak—could potentially interface with systems like this.

Not overpower them.

But perhaps guide them.

Stabilize them.

Or redirect tiny flows.

Just as you nudged the lattice strand beneath the tower.

The Shrine Sleeps

The lantern continues burning quietly above the altar.

Its light flickers across the empty pews.

The guards outside the witch’s door shift in their chairs.

One yawns.

The witch herself is still awake.

Her thoughts moving restlessly in the darkness.

What do you do now?
Visit the witch’s mind, carefully brushing the surface of her thoughts.
Study the lantern longer, experimenting with shaping divine energy around it.
Return to the gem, checking whether the envoy’s divine senses react to anything.
Explore the town, entering the dreams of sleeping villagers.
Examine the shrine wards, learning how they detect corruption and undead.
examine the shrine wards

You drift away from the lantern’s warm glow and let your awareness spread through the stonework of the shrine itself.

The wards are not concentrated in one place like the relic or the flame.

They are woven through the building.

You begin following them.

The Foundation Lines

Beneath the floor, faint divine channels run through the stone foundation.

Not carved deeply—more like thin grooves etched during construction.

These lines connect the reliquary beneath the altar to several key structural points:

• the main doorway
• the outer walls
• the prayer hall floor
• the guest cell corridor

The relic radiates stability, and these lines carry that presence outward, saturating the building with sanctified resonance.

It’s subtle.

But persistent.

The Door Thresholds

The strongest ward sits across the entrance.

A thin band of consecrated stone sits beneath the threshold plank.

When someone crosses the doorway, the ward briefly samples the spiritual resonance of whatever enters.

You feel how it works.

It does not judge morality.

It looks for:

• undead resonance
• necromantic bindings
• corrupted spirits

If something matches those patterns, the ward sends a pulse through the foundation lines.

The priest would feel it.

The lantern flame would flare.

Why It Didn’t Detect You

Your disguise saved you.

The gem appears to contain the scar of a burned-out soul battery, something common in necromantic artifacts.

Dead.

Empty.

Harmless.

To the shrine wards, the gem is just an inert object carried by a living man.

And your true presence is hidden behind the same illusion that fooled the envoy earlier.

The Chapel Field

Inside the prayer hall the wards create a faint field.

You feel it pressing gently against your anchor network.

Not hostile.

But clarifying.

It strengthens divine energy.

And weakens necromantic constructs.

If you were still bound only by the witch’s original soul-binding…

You suspect it would hurt.

But your distributed anchor network—especially the bone anchors—makes your existence more stable and less purely necromantic.

Which is why the shrine tolerates you.

Barely.

The Witch’s Cell

One ward line runs beneath the hallway floor.

It passes directly beneath the door of the witch’s chamber.

Not a prison spell.

But a watch line.

If she performs a ritual inside that room, the line will carry the disturbance straight to the altar.

A quiet alarm system.

A Useful Insight

As you study the ward system, you recognize something familiar.

Like the lattice beneath the tower…

Like your bone anchors…

This shrine works through distributed stability.

One relic.

Many lines.

Balanced pressure.

The same architectural principle repeated again and again.

Whoever first understood that principle changed the way magic could interact with the world.

The shrine continues its quiet vigil.

The lantern burns.

The relic radiates.

The wards breathe gently through the stone.

And down the hallway…

The witch finally lies down on her cot.

Though her mind is still turning slowly in the dark.

What do you do next?
Brush the edge of the witch’s mind, seeing what she’s thinking before sleep.
Study the shrine wards deeper, experimenting with how divine lines react to you.
Return to the gem, checking if the envoy senses anything unusual.
Drift into the town, entering the dreams of sleeping villagers.
Rest within your anchors, letting the network stabilize after the day’s discoveries.
using what i learned from the temple reliquary, flame and wards, i turn to my bones

Flowing.

Less strained.

The seam does not resist your presence.

Deeper Stone

Stone thickens around you. The fracture narrows into a faint crystalline vein running through the bedrock.

This is part of the larger lattice structure you studied beneath the tower.

Even here—far from the main fracture—the strands of the ancient system still guide the pressure of the reservoir sideways through the earth.

Most of the lattice lines remain perfectly aligned.

Whoever built them knew exactly how to balance the enormous force below.

The Old Foundations

Eventually you reach something unexpected.

A buried anchor point.

Long ago—perhaps centuries or millennia—a structure once stood on this hill.

The remains are deep now, collapsed and swallowed by soil and roots.

But its foundation stones still sit here.

Carved with worn divine sigils.

Very similar to the shrine’s architecture… but much older.

This place was once part of the same network of stabilizing sites.

A guardian point for the lattice.

But the structure above it is gone.

Only the bones of the witch’s hill remain.

The Dormant Node

The old foundation stone still touches the lattice.

But without priests, without ritual maintenance, its divine resonance faded long ago.

It is now a dormant node.

Not broken.

Just asleep.

Your bone anchors have unknowingly taken its place as the stabilizing presence on the hill.

Your network and the ancient node share the same location.

The same geometry.

The same purpose.

Far Below

If you push your senses even deeper…

You begin to feel the distant presence again.

The reservoir.

Far away under the tower.

Still vast.

Still patient.

And beneath that…

The faintest suggestion of something even older.

A presence so slow and deep it barely registers as thought.

You wisely do not disturb it.

The Hill Now

You withdraw slightly, returning to the seam where your bones rest above.

The realization settles quietly:

This hill was never random.

Long ago it was one of the stabilizing points in the ancient lattice system.

The witch unknowingly built her hut on top of it.

And now…

Your soul network has begun acting as its replacement anchor.

A new guardian for the seam.

The Shape of the Node

The node is not a single stone.

It is a foundation pattern.

Several large stones arranged in a circular formation roughly the size of a small hut.

At the center lies a square keystone slab.

From that slab radiate four carved channels, forming a cross-like structure embedded into the bedrock.

These channels once carried divine resonance outward through the surrounding ground.

Now they are silent.

But the geometry remains perfect.

The Channels

You follow each channel carefully.

Each one extends several feet outward before merging with the natural fractures in the stone.

Those fractures connect to the larger lattice beneath the earth.

So the node once functioned as a local regulator.

Not sealing the reservoir itself.

But balancing pressure where the lattice came closest to the surface.

The tower covers the main fracture.

This hill covers a secondary seam.

The Keystone

At the center lies the most important part.

A flat square slab with worn divine carvings.

These carvings are extremely old.

Older than the shrine.

Older than the tower.

Their structure resembles the shrine reliquary’s divine geometry—but far more complex.

This stone was likely once paired with a relic, lantern, or priestly presence.

Without it, the node went dormant.

The divine lines lost their power.

But the architecture itself never broke.

How It Relates to You

You compare the layout to your bone network.

Something becomes very clear.

Your anchors accidentally mimic the node’s structure.

Pelvis → central keystone.

Rib / Femur / Skull → directional stabilizers.

Gem → external power source.

You unknowingly built a living version of the node.

Not identical.

But compatible.

The Current State

Right now the node is:

• intact
• dormant
• connected to the lattice
• lacking divine energy

But because your anchors sit within its geometry…

The system is beginning to wake slightly.

Not as a shrine.

Not as a temple.

But as a stabilizing presence again.

The four stone channels do not align with the hill’s terrain.

They align with cardinal directions.

South.

West.

The tower was simply the most dangerous point.

The old node rests beneath the hill.

Not much.

But enough to matter.

How It Fails

You follow the flow of energy through the strand.

Before the ritual, the strand acted like a smooth channel, carrying pressure sideways into neighboring strands.

The surrounding strands compensate.

But the imbalance remains.

To fully repair the strand, something would have to rebuild the missing geometry.

Not simply move it back into place.

Recreate the divine structure that once existed there.

• deeper understanding of the lattice’s original design
• stronger divine resonance than you currently possess
• or another stabilizing node to help carry the strain

Right now you could try to force it.

Because the moment is fun.

Because nothing about it threatens him.

A Small Seed

Somewhere deep in his mind a tiny impression forms.

Not a memory.

Just a vague feeling.

Strange music from far places can be wonderful.

Perhaps tomorrow he will hum a tune he doesn’t remember learning.

The tavern roars with laughter and music.

The guard lifts his mug toward you.

“To good company!”

The dream continues happily around you.

when everyone starts telling tales i tell a story of a young kobold sold away and never seen again, but he might become something later on 

The tavern grows louder as the night rolls on.

Ale flows. Boots thump against the wooden floor. The strange, lively kobold rhythm you introduced has taken hold of the room, and the soldiers now clap and laugh whenever the tune loops around again.

Eventually the music softens.

Someone leans back in their chair and shouts:

“Stories!”

Another soldier bangs his mug against the table.

“Aye! Everyone’s got one!”

The guard whose dream you share grins and points across the table.

“You first, little lizard!”

In dreams, this feels natural.

So you begin.

The Story

You climb onto the table, small claws tapping the wood.

The fire crackles.

Tankards quiet.

And you speak.

“Once there was a young kobold,” you begin.

Your voice is light at first, the way stories are meant to start.

“He lived in tunnels with his kin, where the stone was warm and the fire pits glowed red at night. He ran through the tunnels with his brothers and sisters and chased cave beetles and listened to the old songs.”

The dream listens.

Even the fiddler pauses.

“But one day the kobold’s tribe was poor,” you continue.

“And traders came with shiny coins and sharp knives and promises.”

The laughter around the table fades slightly.

“The tribe sold the kobold to the trader.”

You shrug lightly.

“Sometimes tribes do that.”

The Road

“The trader took the kobold far away. Over hills and forests he had never seen before.”

“The kobold got very hungry.”

A soldier across the table frowns a little.

Another mutters quietly, “That’s rough.”

You nod.

“But the trader sold the kobold again.”

“To a witch.”

The Quiet

The tavern dream grows quieter now.

Even in dreams, people recognize the shape of darker stories.

“So the witch fed the kobold stew,” you say softly.

“And the kobold thought maybe things would be alright.”

You tap the table once with a claw.

“But the witch needed magic.”

The soldiers lean forward slightly.

“So she killed the kobold and took his soul.”

The Turn

For a moment the tavern dream goes very still.

But then you grin.

A small kobold grin.

“But the story doesn’t end there.”

You point toward the ceiling where the music had been playing earlier.

“Because the kobold learned things.”

“How magic works.”

“How bones remember.”

“How dreams open doors.”

The soldiers blink.

The guard you inhabit laughs uncertainly.

“Sounds like the start of a ghost story.”

The Ending

You hop down from the table.

“And maybe one day,” you say, “that kobold will become something else.”

“Something the witch didn’t expect.”

“Something the world hasn’t seen before.”

You lift your mug.

“To kobolds.”

The Dream Responds

For a moment the tavern is silent.

Then one soldier snorts.

“Ha!”

Another raises his mug.

“To the little bastard!”

Laughter returns.

Someone claps you on the back.

“Good story!”

The dream accepts it.

Just another tavern tale.

But deep in the guard’s mind…

The story settles.

Not as truth.

Not as memory.

Just as a strange, haunting little story about a kobold who might not be gone.

The music begins again.

Ale flows.

And the guard’s dream continues warmly around you.

Foam spills.

The dream carries on.

The Night Passes

Dreams do not follow time the way waking life does.

Moments stretch.

Stories repeat.

Songs change and return again.

You watch.

You listen.

You exist.

And for the first time since the night of your death, the memory of fear and knives and binding rituals feels distant.

Here there is only music and laughter.

The Slow Morning

Eventually the dream begins to thin.

Not abruptly.

Gradually.

The tavern lights dim.

The music slows.

The dream figures begin to blur at the edges.

The guard’s body shifts on the bench outside the witch’s cell.

Morning approaches.

His mind prepares to wake.

The tavern fades like mist in sunlight.

Back in the Shrine

The corridor returns.

Cold stone.

Quiet breathing.

The witch is awake again.

Sitting on the edge of her cot.

Waiting.

The ancient node you awakened hums quietly in the earth.

She is already awake.

The Witch

She sits on the narrow cot with her hands loosely resting in her lap, chains hanging slack from her wrists.

Her posture is calm.

Too calm for someone who has spent the night in a locked cell.

Her mind was working even in sleep.

She is thinking about it again.

A statement.

The bolt slides.

Where the pouch containing the gem had rested.

Wind moves through the hills. Insects buzz in the grasses. Somewhere high above, wings beat against the sky.

You reach for that movement.

The Bird

A hawk glides over the hills.

Its wings barely move as it rides the rising thermals. Its mind is sharp, narrow, and intensely focused—nothing like a human mind.

You touch it.

Instantly the world changes.

Hawk Sight

Vision explodes outward.

Where human eyes see fields and roads, the hawk sees motion and shape.

Every small movement below catches attention:

• mice rustling in grass
• rabbits shifting under brush
• the slow line of riders moving along the road

The hawk’s mind is simple but precise.

Hunt.

Glide.

Watch.

You do not try to control it. Instead you ride along with its instincts, letting it carry you higher.

The World From Above

The hills spread beneath you like waves of green and brown.

The road cuts through them in a pale line.

The escort is easy to spot—eight riders moving together with a slower horse in the center carrying the witch.

Farther ahead…

The land opens.

The Capital

From this height you finally see it clearly.

The capital city rises beyond the hills like a stone island.

Massive outer walls encircle it, thick and high enough that even from the air they dominate the landscape.

A wide river curves around one side of the city.

A long stone bridge crosses it toward the main gate.

Inside the walls you can see dense clusters of buildings.

And above them all…

The cathedral.

It towers over the entire city.

White stone.

Great bell towers.

Flying buttresses arching like wings along the sides.

Even the hawk’s instincts notice it as a landmark.

Something Beneath

Your awareness brushes the ground beneath the city as the hawk circles.

The lattice beneath the land is stronger here.

Much stronger than the hill node.

There is another major convergence point under the capital.

Not identical to the tower.

But similar.

The cathedral sits almost directly above it.

The Hawk Turns

The hawk begins drifting back toward the hills, following the rising currents.

Its mind is already losing interest in the distant city.

It has spotted movement in a meadow below.

Prey.

Its instincts sharpen.

What do you do?
Stay with the hawk longer, observing the capital from the air.
Return to the riders, continuing to watch the witch and guards.
Follow the lattice beneath the capital, sensing the node under the cathedral.
Jump to another bird flying toward the city, scouting farther ahead.
Touch the mind of someone inside the city, exploring the capital directly.
i jump to a bird heading towards the city

You release the hunting hawk as it folds its wings and drops toward the meadow.

Your awareness lifts again into the currents of the sky.

For a moment you drift through the air itself—wind over the hills, the scent of grass and dust rising from the road far below.

Then you feel another mind.

Smaller.

Lighter.

Moving toward the city.

You slip into it.

The New Bird

This one is not a hawk.

A crow.

Its wings beat steadily as it flies toward the capital walls.

The mind is different too.

Not purely instinct like the hawk.

There is curiosity here.

Awareness.

Crows remember things.

Notice patterns.

Steal interesting objects.

Your presence settles into its thoughts easily.

The Approach

The city grows larger quickly.

From the crow’s height the capital spreads across the valley like a great stone hive.

Walls thicker than any structure you’ve seen before rise high above the surrounding fields.

Guard towers stand every few hundred paces.

Banner flags snap in the wind above the gatehouses.

The crow circles once as it approaches.

Below you see the main road bridge crossing the river.

Caravans line up outside the gates waiting for entry.

Merchants.

Farmers.

Travelers.

A long slow queue.

Your riders will reach it later today.

Over the Walls

The crow slips easily over the outer wall.

Guards barely glance upward.

Birds pass overhead all the time.

Inside the city the world becomes dense and chaotic.

The Capital

Your crow’s eyes take in the sprawling maze below.

• Narrow streets packed with people
• Market squares bursting with stalls
• Smoke rising from dozens of bakeries and forges
• Temple bells ringing in the distance

The noise of thousands of voices rolls upward in a constant murmur.

The crow banks toward the highest structure in the city.

The cathedral.

The Cathedral

From above it is enormous.

The stone roof spreads like the wings of a giant bird.

Tall towers rise at the corners.

Stained glass windows blaze with morning light.

Wide steps descend into the great square before it.

Pilgrims kneel there even now.

Priests move through the crowds.

Guards patrol the perimeter.

Beneath the Cathedral

Even from the air, you feel it.

The lattice node beneath the building.

Far stronger than the hill node you awakened.

Multiple channels converge here.

This is one of the major anchors of the ancient system.

Not damaged.

Not dormant.

But heavily reinforced.

Layers of divine architecture surround it.

Whatever lies beneath the cathedral…

The church has spent centuries building around it.

The Crow Lands

Your bird lands on a stone gargoyle along the cathedral tower.

From here you can see the entire square.

Pilgrims.

Priests.

Watch patrols.

Merchants.

And the great cathedral doors below.

Somewhere under that building lies the node the guards were talking about.

And the sealed tunnels the traveler remembered.

What do you do next?
Explore the cathedral roof and towers through the crow’s eyes.
Follow the lattice beneath the cathedral, sensing the structure underground.
Drop into the mind of a priest below, learning what the church knows.
Watch the city square, studying the rhythms of the capital.
Return to the riders, who are still approaching the city gates.
i drop into the mind of one of the priests below

You release the crow’s attention from the square below.

For a moment you hover between instincts—the bird’s curiosity about crumbs and shining objects, and your own focus on the structure beneath the cathedral.

Then you descend.

Not physically.

Mentally.

Your awareness stretches from the crow on the gargoyle down into the square.

Thousands of minds move below like a shifting tide.

Merchants arguing over prices.

Pilgrims whispering prayers.

Children chasing each other through the crowd.

You choose carefully.

Not a guard.

Not someone alert.

A priest.

Entering the Priest’s Mind

He stands near the cathedral steps speaking quietly to a small group of pilgrims.

Middle-aged.

Calm.

Disciplined.

His mind is structured very differently from the guards you’ve touched.

There are layers here.

Habit.

Prayer.

Doctrine.

His thoughts move in ordered patterns.

But he is not on alert.

You slip into the edge of his mind like a whisper between breaths.

His Immediate Thoughts

You feel his focus first.

Pilgrims from the south again.

Need to remind them of the midday service.

He gestures calmly while speaking to the group.

His voice carries a practiced warmth.

“Offer your prayers inside and keep the aisles clear for the noon bells.”

The pilgrims thank him and move toward the cathedral doors.

The Cathedral in His Mind

Your awareness drifts deeper.

This priest knows the cathedral intimately.

You see the structure through his memories.

Massive halls.

High vaulted ceilings.

The echo of footsteps across polished stone.

But the most interesting thoughts lie below the surface floors.

The Lower Levels

He remembers walking through stone corridors beneath the cathedral.

Wide crypt chambers filled with ancient tombs.

Engineers working among scaffolding and carved pillars.

Stone blocks being lowered through shafts from above.

But even deeper than the crypts…

There are sealed passages.

Heavy iron gates.

Locked doors marked with temple sigils.

Places ordinary priests do not enter.

The Reason

One memory surfaces clearly.

The priest standing with a senior cleric years ago.

He had asked about the sealed levels.

The older cleric answered quietly.

“Those halls are not for us.”

“Why not?”

“Because they belong to the foundation engineers.”

The Realization

In the priest’s understanding, the cathedral is not simply a temple.

It is also a structure maintaining something below.

Most clergy treat it as sacred mystery.

The engineers handle the practical details.

Few people ever see the deeper chambers.

A Final Thought

As the priest finishes guiding the pilgrims toward the doors, another quiet thought crosses his mind.

The engineers have been working more often lately.

Something about pressure in the foundations.

He does not understand the meaning.

He simply hopes they solve whatever problem exists.

Above him the crow shifts on the gargoyle.

Below, the cathedral doors open as pilgrims enter.

And somewhere beneath that immense building…

The largest lattice node in the region hums quietly under layers of stone and faith.

What do you do next?
Explore deeper into the priest’s memories, searching for the hidden passages below the cathedral.
Leave the priest and jump into the mind of a cathedral engineer, who may know more.
Follow the lattice beneath the cathedral, sensing how it connects to the tower and hill.
Watch the cathedral square, learning how the city moves during the day.
Return to the riders, who are approaching the capital gates.
i gently probe his thoughts.. 'were the wards checked today?'

You remain careful.

The priest’s mind is disciplined, layered with habit and prayer. You cannot push hard here without risking detection.

So you do something gentler.

You shape a thought the way wind shapes the surface of water.

Not an intrusion.

Just a question drifting upward through his attention.

Were the wards checked today?

The Priest Reacts

His steps slow slightly on the cathedral stairs.

Just half a heartbeat.

He doesn’t stop speaking to the pilgrims, but the thought catches his attention.

The wards…

His mind turns toward the idea as if remembering a task.

Not suspicion.

Just routine concern.

His Memory Responds

The thought pulls a recent memory forward.

Early this morning.

Before dawn.

The cathedral’s foundation engineers and two senior clergy were already awake.

You see it through his memory:

A narrow stone stair descending beneath the crypts.

Torches burning along the walls.

A circular chamber carved into ancient bedrock.

In the center of the chamber lies a massive carved ring of stone etched with divine geometry.

The lattice node.

Even larger than the tower’s.

The Inspection

Several robed engineers kneel beside the ring studying its glowing channels.

One of them speaks quietly.

“Pressure stabilized overnight.”

Another replies.

“Yes… but something changed.”

The senior priest present frowns.

“What changed?”

The engineer gestures toward the glowing lines in the stone.

“One of the outer nodes came online.”

The Node

Another engineer kneels closer to the ring.

“See this pressure redistribution?”

He traces a glowing line leading outward through the lattice.

“That node was dormant for centuries.”

The senior priest asks quietly:

“What woke it?”

The engineer shakes his head.

“No idea.”

But his voice carries something else.

Not fear.

Excitement.

The Present Moment

Back in the square, the priest you inhabit finishes guiding the pilgrims toward the cathedral entrance.

The thought settles in his mind.

Yes… the engineers checked the wards this morning.

He adjusts his robes slightly.

Then another thought follows.

Strange that the foundations shifted overnight.

He doesn’t know why.

But you do.

Above him, the crow ruffles its feathers on the gargoyle.

Inside the city walls, thousands of lives continue their daily routines.

And far away beneath a quiet forest hill…

The node you awakened is now part of the cathedral’s calculations.

What do you do next?
Probe deeper into the priest’s memories, learning more about the underground chamber.
Jump into the mind of one of the cathedral engineers, who understands the lattice better.
Follow the lattice connection between the cathedral and your hill node, mapping the network.
Watch the cathedral entrance, studying the flow of clergy and pilgrims.
Return to the riders, who are nearing the city gates.
i use the thought he had of the wards to try and probe what he knows about the wards

You keep the contact light.

The priest’s mind is disciplined, and pressing too hard could trigger instinctive prayer or alertness. Instead you let his own earlier thought—the wards—become the doorway.

You nudge the thought gently.

Not tell me about the wards.

Just let the curiosity expand.

The wards… how are they maintained again?

The Priest’s Knowledge

His mind answers naturally, pulling familiar teachings forward.

The cathedral’s wards are not a single spell.

They are a layered system.

He recalls the basic structure the clergy are taught.

Three levels of protection:

Sanctified Cathedral Grounds
Blessings woven into the stone foundations.
Strengthened by daily prayers and relics in the altar.
Designed to weaken undead and corrupted magic.
The Foundation Rings
The ancient structure beneath the cathedral.
Maintained by the temple engineers.
These are not purely divine wards—they are structural stabilizers tied to the land itself.
The Deep Seal
Something far below the crypts.
The priest does not know its details.
Only senior clergy and engineers descend that far.
What He Does Know

The priest remembers the warning given during his training.

The instructor’s voice echoes in his memory:

“Do not disturb the engineers while they work below.”

“If the lower wards ever fail…”

“…the entire cathedral must be evacuated immediately.”

The Fear Behind the Teaching

The priest never asked what would happen if they failed.

But the implication was clear.

The foundation rings are not protecting the cathedral.

The cathedral is protecting something else.

The Node

His memory briefly returns to the chamber he saw earlier.

The massive carved ring in the stone.

Channels glowing with divine geometry.

Engineers kneeling beside it.

And the line leading outward through the lattice.

The one that shifted when your hill node awakened.

The Priest’s Conclusion

His mind settles the thought with quiet reassurance.

The engineers said it stabilized.

So everything must be fine.

He adjusts his robes and continues greeting pilgrims entering the cathedral.

He never suspects that the cause of the change is currently sitting on a gargoyle above him… watching through a crow.

The Cathedral Square

Below you the city moves in its morning rhythm.

Pilgrims pass through the doors.

Merchants shout across the market.

Temple bells ring faintly.

But now you know something important.

The cathedral is not just built on a lattice node.

It was built to guard it.

What do you do next?
Probe deeper for the “deep seal”, trying to uncover what lies beneath the node.
Jump into the mind of a cathedral engineer, who actually maintains the structure.
Follow the lattice connection beneath the cathedral, mapping the network further.
Watch the cathedral entrance, observing who is allowed inside.

i explore the cathedral itself, and check the wards to see if they might be a problem

You leave the priest’s mind gently.

His thoughts settle back into their orderly rhythm—greeting pilgrims, recalling prayers, keeping the daily flow of the cathedral smooth.

Your awareness rises again into the crow perched high on the gargoyle.

From there, you begin to explore the cathedral itself.

The Outer Wards

You start with the edges.

The cathedral is wrapped in a wide sanctified field, similar to the roadside shrine you studied earlier—but vastly stronger.

Where the shrine used:

• one relic
• a lantern flame
• simple foundation lines

The cathedral uses dozens of relic anchors.

You feel them beneath the building like bright coals buried in stone.

Finger bones of saints.

Fragments of old robes.

Ancient reliquaries sealed into the walls.

Each one radiates divine resonance that flows through the cathedral’s architecture.

Together they form the outer ward field.

How the Field Behaves

You carefully let the ward field brush against your presence.

It reacts the same way the shrine’s did.

Not hostile.

Just… clarifying.

Your distributed anchor network helps again.

Because your existence is no longer purely necromantic.

You are:

• soul
• structure
• lattice anchor

The wards sense something unusual about you.

But not something evil.

Not something that must be destroyed.

For now, they simply do not notice you clearly enough to react.

The Inner Wards

The deeper layers are stronger.

Inside the cathedral walls, divine geometry is carved into pillars, floors, and archways.

These runes serve two purposes:

Support the sanctified field
Detect corruption or necromantic disturbance

If something like the witch’s soul-binding rituals were attempted here…

The entire building would respond.

But your presence remains quiet and hidden.

Your disguise as a burned-out stone still masks the gem.

And the rest of you exists far away through the bone anchors.

The Foundation Rings

You reach deeper.

Below the cathedral floor.

Below the crypts.

Where the engineers work.

Here the magic changes.

This is no longer purely divine warding.

This is structural magic.

Ancient.

Older than the cathedral itself.

The foundation rings are enormous carved circles in the bedrock that interface directly with the lattice node beneath the city.

They do not attack or repel anything.

They simply maintain balance.

Pressure.

Flow.

Distribution.

They are cousins to the node beneath your hill.

But far more complex.

The Good News

After studying the system carefully…

You realize something important.

The cathedral wards are not designed to detect souls like yours.

They are designed to detect:

• undead manifestations
• active necromantic rituals
• corrupted spirits

You are none of those things anymore.

Your existence has become something closer to a living node in the lattice.

To the cathedral system, you resemble infrastructure.

Not a threat.

The Only Risk

There is one possible danger.

The engineers.

If one of them studied the lattice flows carefully enough…

They might notice the new node that awakened in the forest.

And begin investigating.

The City Below

The cathedral square bustles with movement beneath you.

Pilgrims pass through the doors.

Priests move between services.

Guards patrol the perimeter.

And somewhere beyond the hills behind you…

The escort carrying the witch continues riding toward the city gates.

They will arrive within the hour.

What do you do next?
Descend toward the foundation chamber, where the engineers study the lattice node.
Watch the cathedral square, learning the rhythms of the capital.
Jump into the mind of a cathedral engineer, gaining deeper knowledge of the lattice.
Follow the lattice beneath the capital, mapping how it connects to other nodes.
Return to the riders, who are about to reach the city gates with the witch.
i return to my gem, and with all the new knowledge of the wards, i work on refining the structures of my rings

You leave the crow on the cathedral tower.

Wind passes through its feathers as your awareness withdraws. The city fades. The vast stone cathedral, the priests, the wards—all of it recedes as you follow the familiar threads of your anchors.

Crow → air currents → distant hills → the riders on the road.

Then finally…

Gem.

Back Inside the Stone

The pouch sways slightly at the envoy’s saddle as the horses climb the final hill toward the capital.

Leather creaks. Hooves crunch on gravel.

Inside the gem, your awareness settles into the familiar structure you have been building for weeks.

Your rings.

The lattice of memory, structure, and protection you wove around yourself.

But now…

You understand far more.

What You Learned

From the shrine:

relic anchors radiate stability
divine flame feeds the structure
wards detect patterns, not intent

From the cathedral:

large structures distribute resonance across many anchors
stabilizing rings redirect pressure rather than resisting it
divine wards ignore stable infrastructure

And from the lattice:

alignment matters more than force
flow must remain smooth
Reworking the Rings

You begin slowly.

The outer ring—the one made from calm memories and simple forms—becomes your stability field.

Instead of merely containing you, it now radiates a quiet balancing presence the way the shrine relic did.

Small.

Subtle.

But constant.

The second ring—the flowing lattice you built from peaceful memories—changes next.

You reshape its channels.

Instead of simply holding energy, they now redirect ambient magic the same way the cathedral foundation rings redirect pressure.

Magic that touches you flows around the core rather than through it.

The third ring, built from the sharp memory of your death…

You refine carefully.

It becomes a filter layer.

Corrupt magic striking the structure will collide with this ring first, where the harsh memory forces the energy to break apart and disperse before reaching deeper layers.

Painful memory becomes armor.

Finally the core ring—the one built from your earliest childhood memories.

You adjust its geometry to mirror the keystone structure beneath the hill.

It becomes the true center.

Not just a container for your soul.

But the stabilizing anchor that holds every other ring in alignment.

The Result

When you finish the adjustments, the entire structure settles.

The rings rotate slowly around the core like quiet celestial bodies.

Memory.

Structure.

Defense.

Flow.

You are no longer just hiding inside a gem.

You are a small, living lattice.

Outside the pouch the riders crest the hill.

Below them the capital spreads wide across the valley.

Stone walls.

The great river.

And the towering cathedral watching over it all.

The escort begins descending toward the gates.

The witch glances at the city with quiet interest.

And inside the gem…

Your structure hums with new stability.

What do you do next?
Observe the capital gates as the riders approach, learning how entry works.

Reach toward the cathedral node, comparing it to the hill node you awakened.

i watch and listen to the guards as we enter the city

The road slopes downward toward the capital.

The riders crest the final hill, and the full scale of the city spreads out before them.

Massive stone walls ring the valley floor. Towers stand every few hundred paces, banners snapping in the morning wind. The river curves around the western side of the city, its surface glittering beneath the long stone bridge that leads to the main gate.

The escort rides in silence for a few minutes as the sight fills the horizon.

Even the guards, who have likely seen it before, sit a little straighter in their saddles.

The Witch’s Reaction

The witch studies the city carefully.

Her eyes move across the walls, the towers, the bridge, and then upward toward the cathedral rising over the rooftops.

That same faint smile returns to her lips.

She recognizes what you sensed from the air.

Structures built on top of older structures.

Mystery layered beneath stone.

But she says nothing.

The Gate Queue

By the time the escort reaches the bridge, a long line has already formed.

Merchants with wagons.

Farmers with livestock.

Travelers on foot.

Guards patrol along the queue, checking documents and occasionally inspecting cargo.

But when the envoy’s banner becomes visible, things change.

A gate officer steps forward.

The Guards Speak

“Envoy,” the officer says, nodding respectfully.

The envoy returns the gesture.

“Prisoner transfer.”

The officer glances toward the witch, taking in the chains and the escort.

“Understood.”

He waves his men aside.

“Clear the road.”

One of the guards behind the witch mutters quietly to another.

“Nice when rank actually does something.”

The other snorts.

“Don’t get used to it.”

Passing the Gate

The heavy wooden gates stand open between two thick towers.

As the riders pass beneath the archway, the sounds of the city swell around them.

Shouting merchants.

Hammering from distant forges.

Cart wheels rattling over stone.

A thousand conversations layered together.

The guards around the witch relax slightly now that they are inside.

One of them gestures toward the towering cathedral.

“Still can’t get over that place.”

Another replies:

“Wait until you see it from inside.”

“You’ve been?”

“Once.”

“And?”

The guard whistles softly.

“Feels like the roof is touching the sky.”

The Witch Listens

The witch glances up at the cathedral again.

Then toward the ground beneath the street.

Then toward the envoy.

Her mind is working constantly now.

She has felt the change in the lattice.

She heard the guards talk about the foundations.

She knows something under the city matters.

But she still doesn’t know what.

Inside the Capital

The escort moves deeper into the city.

Narrow streets wind between tall buildings.

Market stalls spill out into the roads.

Citizens step aside quickly when they see the armed riders escorting a chained prisoner.

And above it all…

The cathedral towers over everything.

Its bells begin ringing the hour.

The sound rolls across the entire city.
